	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Warsaw</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>
		
		
		
		<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>
		<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>
		<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Capital of Poland</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about the Polish capital. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Warsaw (disambiguation)">Warsaw (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"Warszawa" redirects here. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Warszawa_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Warszawa (disambiguation)">Warszawa (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"City of Warsaw" redirects here. For the Second World War fighter squadron, see <a href="/wiki/No._316_Polish_Fighter_Squadron" title="No. 316 Polish Fighter Squadron">No. 316 Polish Fighter Squadron</a>. For the airplane that crossed the Atlantic in 1934, see <a href="/wiki/Adamowicz_brothers" title="Adamowicz brothers">Adamowicz brothers</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">
</p>

<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><div class="mediaContainer" style="width:220px"><audio id="mwe_player_0" controls="" preload="none" style="width:220px" class="kskin" data-durationhint="44.982857142857" data-startoffset="0" data-mwtitle="Hejnal_Warszawski.ogg" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons"><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/ff/Hejnal_Warszawski.ogg" type="audio/ogg; codecs=&quot;vorbis&quot;" data-title="Original Ogg file (117 kbps)" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="117107" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/f/ff/Hejnal_Warszawski.ogg/Hejnal_Warszawski.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg" data-title="MP3" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="169848" /></audio></div>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hejnal_Warszawski.ogg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Varsovian Trumpet Call</div></div></div>
<p><b>Warsaw</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;w&#39; in &#39;wind&#39;">w</span><span title="/ɔːr/: &#39;ar&#39; in &#39;war&#39;">ɔːr</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="/ɔː/: &#39;au&#39; in &#39;fraud&#39;">ɔː</span></span>/</a></span></span> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i title="English pronunciation respelling"><span style="font-size:90%">WOR</span>-saw</i></a>; <a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">Polish</a>: <i lang="pl">Warszawa</i> <span class="IPA" style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Polish" title="Help:IPA/Polish">[varˈʂava]</a></span>&#32;<span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pl-Warszawa.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/01/Pl-Warszawa.ogg" class="internal" title="Pl-Warszawa.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span>; see also <a href="#Etymology_and_names">other names</a>) is the capital and <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_and_towns_in_Poland" title="List of cities and towns in Poland">largest city</a> of <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>. The metropolis stands on the <a href="/wiki/Vistula" title="Vistula">Vistula</a> River in east-central Poland and its population is officially estimated at 1.78&#160;million residents within a <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_metropolitan_area" title="Warsaw metropolitan area">greater metropolitan area</a> of 3.1&#160;million residents,<sup id="cite_ref-larger_urban_zone_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-larger_urban_zone-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> which makes Warsaw the <a href="/wiki/Largest_capital_cities_of_the_European_Union" title="Largest capital cities of the European Union">8th most-populous capital city</a> in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>. The city limits cover 517.24 square kilometres (199.71&#160;sq&#160;mi), while the metropolitan area covers 6,100.43 square kilometres (2,355.39&#160;sq&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-goeuro2012_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-goeuro2012-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Warsaw is an <a href="/wiki/Global_city" title="Global city">alpha global city</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> a major international tourist destination, and a significant cultural, political and <a href="/wiki/Financial_centre" title="Financial centre">economic hub</a>. Its historical <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Old_Town" title="Warsaw Old Town">old town</a> was designated a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCO World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage Site</a>.
</p><p>Once described as the "Paris of the North", Warsaw was believed to be one of the most beautiful cities in the world until <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Bombed at the start of the <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Poland" title="Invasion of Poland">German invasion</a> in 1939, the city <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Warsaw_(1939)" title="Siege of Warsaw (1939)">withstood a siege</a> for which it was later awarded Poland's highest military decoration for heroism, the <a href="/wiki/Virtuti_Militari" title="Virtuti Militari">Virtuti Militari</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-coat_of_arms_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coat_of_arms-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Czerkawski_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Czerkawski-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Deportations of the Jewish population to concentration camps led to the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Ghetto_Uprising" title="Warsaw Ghetto Uprising">Warsaw Ghetto Uprising</a> in 1943 and the destruction of the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Ghetto" title="Warsaw Ghetto">Ghetto</a> after a month of combat. A general <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Uprising" title="Warsaw Uprising">Warsaw Uprising</a> between August and October 1944 led to even greater devastation and <a href="/wiki/Planned_destruction_of_Warsaw" class="mw-redirect" title="Planned destruction of Warsaw">systematic razing by the Germans</a> in advance of the <a href="/wiki/Vistula%E2%80%93Oder_Offensive" title="Vistula–Oder Offensive">Vistula–Oder Offensive</a>. Warsaw gained the new title of <i>Phoenix City</i> because of its extensive <a href="/wiki/History_of_Warsaw" title="History of Warsaw">history</a> and complete reconstruction after World War II, which had left over 85% of its buildings in ruins.<sup id="cite_ref-setac_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-setac-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-miastofeniksa_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-miastofeniksa-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Warsaw is one of Europe's most dynamic metropolitan cities.<sup id="cite_ref-msz.gov.pl_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-msz.gov.pl-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> In 2012 the <a href="/wiki/Economist_Intelligence_Unit" title="Economist Intelligence Unit">Economist Intelligence Unit</a> ranked Warsaw as the <a href="/wiki/World%27s_most_liveable_cities" class="mw-redirect" title="World&#39;s most liveable cities">32nd most liveable city</a> in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-pages.eiu.com_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pages.eiu.com-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> In 2017 the city came 4th in the "Business-friendly" category and 8th in "Human capital and life style".<sup id="cite_ref-msz.gov.pl_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-msz.gov.pl-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> It was also ranked as one of the most liveable cities in <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central</a> and Eastern Europe.
</p><p>The city is a significant centre of research and development, <a href="/wiki/Business_process_outsourcing" class="mw-redirect" title="Business process outsourcing">Business process outsourcing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Information_technology_outsourcing" class="mw-redirect" title="Information technology outsourcing">Information technology outsourcing</a>, as well as of the Polish media industry. The <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Stock_Exchange" title="Warsaw Stock Exchange">Warsaw Stock Exchange</a> is the largest and most important in <a href="/wiki/Central_and_Eastern_Europe" title="Central and Eastern Europe">Central and Eastern Europe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Frontex" class="mw-redirect" title="Frontex">Frontex</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Agencies_of_the_European_Union" title="Agencies of the European Union">European Union agency</a> for external border security as well as <a href="/wiki/ODIHR" class="mw-redirect" title="ODIHR">ODIHR</a>, one of the principal institutions of the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Cooperation_in_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Organization for Security and Cooperation in Europe">Organization for Security and Cooperation in Europe</a> have their headquarters in Warsaw. Together with Frankfurt, London and Paris, Warsaw is also one of the cities with the highest number of skyscrapers in the European Union.<sup id="cite_ref-scraper_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scraper-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The city is the seat of the <a href="/wiki/Polish_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Polish Academy of Sciences">Polish Academy of Sciences</a>, <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_National_Philharmonic_Orchestra" title="Warsaw National Philharmonic Orchestra">Warsaw National Philharmonic Orchestra</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Warsaw" title="University of Warsaw">University of Warsaw</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_University_of_Technology" title="Warsaw University of Technology">Warsaw University of Technology</a>, the <a href="/wiki/National_Museum,_Warsaw" title="National Museum, Warsaw">National Museum</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Theatre,_Warsaw" title="Grand Theatre, Warsaw">Great Theatre—National Opera</a>, the largest of its kind in the world,<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Zach%C4%99ta" title="Zachęta">Zachęta</a> National Gallery of Art. The picturesque <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Old_Town" title="Warsaw Old Town">Old Town of Warsaw</a>, which represents examples of nearly every European architectural style and <a href="/wiki/List_of_time_periods" title="List of time periods">historical period</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> was listed as a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCO World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> in 1980. Other main architectural attractions include the <a href="/wiki/Castle_Square,_Warsaw" title="Castle Square, Warsaw">Castle Square</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Castle,_Warsaw" title="Royal Castle, Warsaw">Royal Castle</a> and the iconic <a href="/wiki/Sigismund%27s_Column" title="Sigismund&#39;s Column">King Sigismund's Column</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Wilan%C3%B3w_Palace" title="Wilanów Palace">Wilanów Palace</a>, the <a href="/wiki/%C5%81azienki_Palace" class="mw-redirect" title="Łazienki Palace">Łazienki Palace</a>, <a href="/wiki/St._John%27s_Cathedral,_Warsaw" class="mw-redirect" title="St. John&#39;s Cathedral, Warsaw">St. John's Cathedral</a>, <a href="/wiki/Old_Town_Market_Place,_Warsaw" title="Old Town Market Place, Warsaw">Main Market Square</a>, <a href="/wiki/Palace" title="Palace">palaces</a>, churches and mansions all displaying a richness of colour and detail. Warsaw is positioning itself as Central and Eastern Europe’s chic cultural capital with thriving art and club scenes and serious restaurants,<sup id="cite_ref-eastern_europe_capital_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eastern_europe_capital-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> with around a quarter of the city's area occupied by parks.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_and_names">Etymology and names</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology and names">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Warsaw's name in the Polish language is <i>Warszawa</i> (also formerly spelled <i>Warszewa</i> and <i>Warszowa</i>). Other previous spellings of the name may have included <i>Worszewa</i> and <i>Werszewa</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> According to some sources,<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> the origin of the name is unknown. In <i>Pre-Slavic toponomastic layer of Northern Mazovia: corrections and addenda (the Narew drainage)</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> it is stated that the toponymy of northern Mazovia tends to have unclear etymology (p.&#160;30). Originally, Warszawa was the name of a fishing village. According to one theory <i>Warszawa</i> means "belonging to Warsz", <i>Warsz</i> being a shortened form of the masculine <a href="/wiki/Slavic_names" title="Slavic names">name of Slavic origin</a> Warcisław; see also etymology of <a href="/wiki/Wroc%C5%82aw" title="Wrocław">Wrocław</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Rymut_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rymut-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> However the ending -awa is unusual for a big city; the names of Polish cities derived from personal names usually ending in -ów/owo/ew/ewo (e.g. Piotrków, Adamów) while the -av- in the early name of Wrocław is part of a personal name. 
</p><p><a href="/wiki/False_etymology" title="False etymology">Folk etymology</a> attributes the city name to a fisherman, Wars, and his wife, Sawa. According to legend, Sawa was a mermaid living in the Vistula River with whom Wars fell in love.<sup id="cite_ref-warsaw-legend_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-warsaw-legend-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> In actuality, Warsz was a 12th/13th-century nobleman who owned a village located at the modern-day site of the <a href="/wiki/Mariensztat" title="Mariensztat">Mariensztat</a> neighbourhood.<sup id="cite_ref-syrenka_historia_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-syrenka_historia-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> See also the <a href="/wiki/Vr%C5%A1ovci" title="Vršovci">Vršovci</a> family which had escaped to Poland. The official city name in full is <i lang="pl" title="Polish language text">miasto stołeczne Warszawa</i> (<i>"The Capital City of Warsaw"</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-prawo_lex_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prawo_lex-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>Other names for Warsaw include <i lang="lt" title="Lithuanian language text">Varsovia</i> (<a href="/wiki/Latin_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin language">Latin</a>, Spanish) and <i>Varsóvia</i> (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>), <i lang="fr" title="French language text">Varsovie</i> (French), <i lang="it" title="Italian language text">Varsavia</i> (Italian), <i lang="de" title="German language text">Warschau</i> (German, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>), <span lang="yi" dir="rtl" title="Yiddish language text">װאַרשע</span> /<i>Varshe</i> (<a href="/wiki/Yiddish_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Yiddish language">Yiddish</a>), <i lang="lt" title="Lithuanian language text">Varšuva</i> (<a href="/wiki/Lithuanian_language" title="Lithuanian language">Lithuanian</a>), <i lang="hu" title="Hungarian language text">Varsó</i> (<a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">Hungarian</a>) and <i>Varšava</i> (<a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">Czech</a>)
</p><p>A native or resident of Warsaw is known as a <i>Varsovian</i> – in Polish <i>warszawiak</i>, <i>warszawianin</i> (male), <i>warszawianka </i>(female), <i>warszawiacy</i>, and <i>warszawianie</i> (plural).
</p>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For the name of Warsaw in various languages, see <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Warsaw" class="extiw" title="wikt:Warsaw">wikt:Warsaw</a>.</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Warsaw" title="History of Warsaw">History of Warsaw</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Warsaw" title="Timeline of Warsaw">Timeline of Warsaw</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hogenberg_View_of_Warsaw_(detail).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Hogenberg_View_of_Warsaw_%28detail%29.jpg/220px-Hogenberg_View_of_Warsaw_%28detail%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="177" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Hogenberg_View_of_Warsaw_%28detail%29.jpg/330px-Hogenberg_View_of_Warsaw_%28detail%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Hogenberg_View_of_Warsaw_%28detail%29.jpg/440px-Hogenberg_View_of_Warsaw_%28detail%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1300" data-file-height="1044" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hogenberg_View_of_Warsaw_(detail).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A paper engraving of 16th-century Warsaw by <a href="/wiki/Frans_Hogenberg" title="Frans Hogenberg">Hogenberg</a> showing <a href="/wiki/St._John%27s_Archcathedral_(Warsaw)" class="mw-redirect" title="St. John&#39;s Archcathedral (Warsaw)">St. John's Archcathedral</a> to the right. The temple was founded in 1390, and is one of the city's ancient and most important landmarks.</div></div></div>
<p>The first fortified settlements on the site of today's Warsaw were located in <a href="/wiki/Br%C3%B3dno" title="Bródno">Bródno</a> (9th/10th century) and <a href="/wiki/Ujazd%C3%B3w_Castle" title="Ujazdów Castle">Jazdów</a> (12th/13th century).<sup id="cite_ref-history_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> After Jazdów was raided by nearby clans and dukes, a new similar settlement was established on the site of a small fishing village called Warszowa. The Prince of <a href="/wiki/P%C5%82ock" title="Płock">Płock</a>, Bolesław II of Masovia, established this settlement, the modern-day Warsaw, in about 1300. In the beginning of the 14th century it became one of the seats of the <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Masovia" title="Duke of Masovia">Dukes of Masovia</a>, becoming the official capital of the Masovian Duchy in 1413.<sup id="cite_ref-history_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> 14th-century Warsaw's economy rested on mostly crafts and trade. Upon the extinction of the local ducal line, the duchy was reincorporated into the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_the_Kingdom_of_Poland" title="Crown of the Kingdom of Poland">Crown of the Kingdom of Poland</a> in 1526.<sup id="cite_ref-history_31-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="16th_to_18th_centuries">16th to 18th centuries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 16th to 18th centuries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bellotto_New_Town_Market_Square.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Bellotto_New_Town_Market_Square.jpg/220px-Bellotto_New_Town_Market_Square.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="174" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Bellotto_New_Town_Market_Square.jpg/330px-Bellotto_New_Town_Market_Square.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Bellotto_New_Town_Market_Square.jpg/440px-Bellotto_New_Town_Market_Square.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="789" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bellotto_New_Town_Market_Square.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Warsaw_New_Town" title="Warsaw New Town">Warsaw New Town</a> in 1778. Painted by <a href="/wiki/Bernardo_Bellotto" title="Bernardo Bellotto">Bernardo Bellotto</a></div></div></div>
<p>In 1529, Warsaw for the first time became the seat of the <a href="/wiki/Sejm_of_the_Republic_of_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="Sejm of the Republic of Poland">General Sejm</a>, permanently from 1569.<sup id="cite_ref-history_31-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> In 1573 the city gave its name to the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Confederation" title="Warsaw Confederation">Warsaw Confederation</a>, formally establishing <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion" title="Freedom of religion">religious freedom</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth" title="Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth">Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth</a>. Due to its central location between the Commonwealth's capitals of <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w" title="Kraków">Kraków</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vilnius" title="Vilnius">Vilnius</a>, Warsaw became the capital of the Commonwealth and the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_the_Kingdom_of_Poland" title="Crown of the Kingdom of Poland">Crown of the Kingdom of Poland</a> when King <a href="/wiki/Sigismund_III_Vasa" title="Sigismund III Vasa">Sigismund III Vasa</a> moved his court from Kraków to Warsaw in 1596.<sup id="cite_ref-history_31-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
In the following years the town expanded towards the suburbs. Several private independent districts were established—the property of aristocrats and the gentry, which they ruled by their own laws. Three times between 1655 and 1658 the city was under siege, and three times it was taken and pillaged by the Swedish, <a href="/wiki/Margraviate_of_Brandenburg" title="Margraviate of Brandenburg">Brandenburgian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Transylvania" title="Transylvania">Transylvanian</a> forces.<sup id="cite_ref-history_31-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ascheron_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ascheron-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1700, the <a href="/wiki/Great_Northern_War" title="Great Northern War">Great Northern War</a> broke out. The city was besieged several times and was obliged to pay heavy tribute.<sup id="cite_ref-timeline_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timeline-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Warsaw turned into an early-<a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">capitalist</a> city. The reign of <a href="/wiki/Augustus_II_the_Strong" title="Augustus II the Strong">Augustus II</a> and <a href="/wiki/Augustus_III_of_Poland" title="Augustus III of Poland">Augustus III</a> was a time of development for Warsaw. The <a href="/wiki/Saxony" title="Saxony">Saxon</a> monarchs brought many renowned German architects, who rebuilt the city in a style similar to <a href="/wiki/Dresden" title="Dresden">Dresden</a>. In 1747 the <a href="/wiki/Za%C5%82uski_Library" title="Załuski Library">Załuski Library</a> was established, the first Polish public library and the largest at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Stanis%C5%82aw_II_Augustus" class="mw-redirect" title="Stanisław II Augustus">Stanisław II Augustus</a>, who remodelled the interior of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Castle,_Warsaw" title="Royal Castle, Warsaw">Royal Castle</a>, also made Warsaw a centre of culture and the arts.<sup id="cite_ref-Rozek_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rozek-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Stanley_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stanley-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> He extended the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Baths_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Baths Park">Royal Baths Park</a> and ordered the construction or refurbishment of numerous palaces, mansions and richly-decorated <a href="/wiki/Tenements" class="mw-redirect" title="Tenements">tenements</a>. This earned Warsaw the nickname <i>Paris of the East</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Golna_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Golna-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Warsaw remained the capital of the Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth until 1795, when it was annexed by the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia" title="Kingdom of Prussia">Kingdom of Prussia</a> in the third and final <a href="/wiki/Partitions_of_Poland" title="Partitions of Poland">partition of Poland</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> it subsequently became the capital of the province of <a href="/wiki/South_Prussia" title="South Prussia">South Prussia</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="19th_and_20th_centuries">19th and 20th centuries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 19th and 20th centuries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Filtry_Warszawskie_przy_ul._Koszykowej_81_w_Warszawie,_Hala_Filtr%C3%B3w_Powolnych.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Filtry_Warszawskie_przy_ul._Koszykowej_81_w_Warszawie%2C_Hala_Filtr%C3%B3w_Powolnych.jpg/220px-Filtry_Warszawskie_przy_ul._Koszykowej_81_w_Warszawie%2C_Hala_Filtr%C3%B3w_Powolnych.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Filtry_Warszawskie_przy_ul._Koszykowej_81_w_Warszawie%2C_Hala_Filtr%C3%B3w_Powolnych.jpg/330px-Filtry_Warszawskie_przy_ul._Koszykowej_81_w_Warszawie%2C_Hala_Filtr%C3%B3w_Powolnych.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Filtry_Warszawskie_przy_ul._Koszykowej_81_w_Warszawie%2C_Hala_Filtr%C3%B3w_Powolnych.jpg/440px-Filtry_Warszawskie_przy_ul._Koszykowej_81_w_Warszawie%2C_Hala_Filtr%C3%B3w_Powolnych.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="667" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Filtry_Warszawskie_przy_ul._Koszykowej_81_w_Warszawie,_Hala_Filtr%C3%B3w_Powolnych.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Water_Filters" title="Warsaw Water Filters">Water Filters</a>, designed by <a href="/wiki/William_Lindley" title="William Lindley">William Lindley</a> and finished in 1886</div></div></div>
<p>Liberated by <a href="/wiki/Napoleon_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Napoleon I">Napoleon</a>'s army in 1806, Warsaw was made the capital of the newly created <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Warsaw" title="Duchy of Warsaw">Duchy of Warsaw</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-history_31-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Following the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Vienna" title="Congress of Vienna">Congress of Vienna</a> of 1815, Warsaw became the centre of <a href="/wiki/Congress_Poland" title="Congress Poland">Congress Poland</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a> under a <a href="/wiki/Personal_union" title="Personal union">personal union</a> with <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Imperial Russia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-history_31-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The Royal University of Warsaw was established in 1816.
</p><p>Following repeated violations of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_the_Kingdom_of_Poland" title="Constitution of the Kingdom of Poland">Polish constitution</a> by the Russians, the 1830 <a href="/wiki/November_uprising" class="mw-redirect" title="November uprising">November uprising</a> broke out. But the Polish-Russian war of 1831 ended in the uprising's defeat and in the curtailment of the Kingdom's autonomy.<sup id="cite_ref-history_31-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> On 27 February 1861 a Warsaw crowd protesting against Russian rule over Poland was fired upon by Russian troops.<sup id="cite_ref-Naliwajek_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Naliwajek-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-obrien_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-obrien-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Five people were killed. The Underground <a href="/wiki/Polish_National_Government_(January_Uprising)" title="Polish National Government (January Uprising)">Polish National Government</a> resided in Warsaw during the <a href="/wiki/January_Uprising" title="January Uprising">January Uprising</a> in 1863–64.<sup id="cite_ref-obrien_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-obrien-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:234px;max-width:234px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/66/Warszawa_-_Marsza%C5%82kowska_1912.jpg/230px-Warszawa_-_Marsza%C5%82kowska_1912.jpg" decoding="async" width="230" height="147" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/66/Warszawa_-_Marsza%C5%82kowska_1912.jpg 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="287" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Marsza%C5%82kowska_Street,_Warsaw" title="Marszałkowska Street, Warsaw">Marszałkowska Street</a> as it appeared in 1912</div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:232px;max-width:232px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Pl_warszawa_filharmonia_old_1918.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Pl_warszawa_filharmonia_old_1918.jpg/230px-Pl_warszawa_filharmonia_old_1918.jpg" decoding="async" width="230" height="143" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Pl_warszawa_filharmonia_old_1918.jpg/345px-Pl_warszawa_filharmonia_old_1918.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Pl_warszawa_filharmonia_old_1918.jpg/460px-Pl_warszawa_filharmonia_old_1918.jpg 2x" data-file-width="535" data-file-height="332" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/National_Philharmonic_in_Warsaw" title="National Philharmonic in Warsaw">Warsaw National Philharmonic</a> in 1918</div></div></div></div></div>
<p>Warsaw flourished in the late 19th century under Mayor <a href="/wiki/Sokrates_Starynkiewicz" title="Sokrates Starynkiewicz">Sokrates Starynkiewicz</a> (1875–92), a Russian-born general appointed by <a href="/wiki/Alexander_III_of_Russia" title="Alexander III of Russia">Tsar Alexander III</a>. Under Starynkiewicz Warsaw saw its first water and sewer systems designed and built by the English engineer <a href="/wiki/William_Lindley" title="William Lindley">William Lindley</a> and his son, <a href="/wiki/William_Heerlein_Lindley" title="William Heerlein Lindley">William Heerlein Lindley</a>, as well as the expansion and modernisation of trams, street lighting, and gas infrastructure.<sup id="cite_ref-history_31-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire_Census" title="Russian Empire Census">Russian Empire Census</a> of 1897 recorded 626,000 people living in Warsaw, making it the third-largest city of the Empire after <a href="/wiki/St._Petersburg" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Petersburg">St. Petersburg</a> and Moscow.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Capital_of_Second_Polish_Republic:_1918.E2.80.9339"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Capital_of_Second_Polish_Republic:_1918–39">Capital of Second Polish Republic: 1918–39</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Capital of Second Polish Republic: 1918–39">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Warsaw was occupied by Germany from 4 August 1915 until November 1918. The Allied Armistice terms required in Article 12 that Germany withdraw from areas controlled by Russia in 1914, which included Warsaw.<sup id="cite_ref-Wandycz_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wandycz-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Germany did so, and underground leader <a href="/wiki/Pi%C5%82sudski" class="mw-redirect" title="Piłsudski">Piłsudski</a> returned to Warsaw on 11 November and set up what became the <a href="/wiki/Second_Polish_Republic" title="Second Polish Republic">Second Polish Republic</a>, with Warsaw as the capital. In the course of the <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Soviet_War" title="Polish–Soviet War">Polish-Bolshevik War</a> of 1920, the huge <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Warsaw_(1920)" title="Battle of Warsaw (1920)">Battle of Warsaw</a> was fought on the eastern outskirts of the city in which the capital was successfully defended and the <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a> defeated. Poland stopped the full brunt of the Red Army by itself and defeated the idea of the "<a href="/wiki/Export_of_revolution" title="Export of revolution">export of the revolution</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-Zamoyski_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zamoyski-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/%C5%9Arednicowy_Bridge" title="Średnicowy Bridge">Średnicowy Bridge</a> was constructed for a railway (1921–1931), connecting both parts of the city. <a href="/wiki/Warszawa_G%C5%82%C3%B3wna_railway_station" title="Warszawa Główna railway station">Warszawa Główna railway station</a> (1932–1939) was unfinished and destroyed during WWII.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Stefan_Starzy%C5%84ski" title="Stefan Starzyński">Stefan Starzyński</a> was the <a href="/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_Warsaw" title="List of mayors of Warsaw">Mayor of Warsaw</a> 1934–1939; he was murdered by the Nazis in December 1939.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_World_War">Second World War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Second World War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Warsaw_Old_Town_1945.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Warsaw_Old_Town_1945.jpg/280px-Warsaw_Old_Town_1945.jpg" decoding="async" width="280" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Warsaw_Old_Town_1945.jpg/420px-Warsaw_Old_Town_1945.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Warsaw_Old_Town_1945.jpg/560px-Warsaw_Old_Town_1945.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2908" data-file-height="1673" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Warsaw_Old_Town_1945.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Destruction_of_Warsaw" title="Destruction of Warsaw">Sea of rubble</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-last_glimpse_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-last_glimpse-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>&#160;– over 85% of the buildings in Warsaw <a href="/wiki/Aftermath_of_the_Warsaw_Uprising" title="Aftermath of the Warsaw Uprising">were destroyed</a> by the end of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Old_Town" title="Warsaw Old Town">Old Town</a> and <a href="/wiki/Royal_Castle,_Warsaw" title="Royal Castle, Warsaw">Royal Castle</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>After the German <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Poland" title="Invasion of Poland">Invasion of Poland</a> on 1 September 1939 started the Second World War, Warsaw <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Warsaw_(1939)" title="Siege of Warsaw (1939)">was defended</a> until 27 September. Central Poland, including Warsaw, came under the rule of the <a href="/wiki/General_Government" title="General Government">General Government</a>, a German <a href="/wiki/Nazism" title="Nazism">Nazi</a> colonial administration. All higher education institutions were immediately closed and Warsaw's entire Jewish population – several hundred thousand, some 30% of the city&#160;&#8211;&#32;were herded into the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Ghetto" title="Warsaw Ghetto">Warsaw Ghetto</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ushmm_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ushmm-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> The city would become the centre of urban resistance to Nazi rule in occupied Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-Snyder_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Snyder-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> When the order came to annihilate the ghetto as part of <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Hitler</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Final_Solution" title="Final Solution">Final Solution</a>" on 19 April 1943, Jewish fighters launched the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Ghetto_uprising" class="mw-redirect" title="Warsaw Ghetto uprising">Warsaw Ghetto uprising</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ghettouprising_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ghettouprising-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Despite being heavily outgunned and outnumbered, the Ghetto held out for almost a month.<sup id="cite_ref-ghettouprising_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ghettouprising-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> When the fighting ended, almost all survivors were massacred, with only a few managing to escape or hide.<sup id="cite_ref-ghettouprising_47-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ghettouprising-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-aish_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aish-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Powstanie_Warszawskie_film_Joachmiczyk.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Powstanie_Warszawskie_film_Joachmiczyk.jpg/220px-Powstanie_Warszawskie_film_Joachmiczyk.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="240" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Powstanie_Warszawskie_film_Joachmiczyk.jpg/330px-Powstanie_Warszawskie_film_Joachmiczyk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Powstanie_Warszawskie_film_Joachmiczyk.jpg/440px-Powstanie_Warszawskie_film_Joachmiczyk.jpg 2x" data-file-width="595" data-file-height="650" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Powstanie_Warszawskie_film_Joachmiczyk.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_uprising" class="mw-redirect" title="Warsaw uprising">Warsaw uprising</a> took place in 1944. The <a href="/wiki/Armia_Krajowa" class="mw-redirect" title="Armia Krajowa">Polish Home Army</a> attempted to liberate Warsaw from German occupation before the arrival of the <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-britannica_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-britannica-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>By July 1944, the <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a> was deep into Polish territory and pursuing the Germans toward Warsaw.<sup id="cite_ref-uprising_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uprising-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Knowing that <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Stalin</a> was hostile to the idea of an independent Poland, the <a href="/wiki/Polish_government-in-exile" title="Polish government-in-exile">Polish government-in-exile</a> in London gave orders to the underground <a href="/wiki/Armia_Krajowa" class="mw-redirect" title="Armia Krajowa">Home Army (AK)</a> to try to seize control of Warsaw from the Germans before the Red Army arrived. Thus, on 1 August 1944, as the Red Army was nearing the city, the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_uprising" class="mw-redirect" title="Warsaw uprising">Warsaw uprising</a> began.<sup id="cite_ref-uprising_50-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uprising-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> The armed struggle, planned to last 48 hours, was partially successful, however it went on for 63 days. Eventually the Home Army fighters and civilians assisting them were forced to capitulate.<sup id="cite_ref-uprising_50-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uprising-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> They were transported to <a href="/wiki/Prisoner_of_war" title="Prisoner of war">PoW</a> camps in Germany, while the entire civilian population was expelled.<sup id="cite_ref-uprising_50-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uprising-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Polish civilian deaths are estimated at between 150,000 and 200,000.<sup id="cite_ref-Borkiewicz_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Borkiewicz-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Hitler, ignoring the agreed terms of the capitulation, ordered the <a href="/wiki/Destruction_of_Warsaw" title="Destruction of Warsaw">entire city to be razed to the ground</a> and the library and museum collections taken to Germany or burned.<sup id="cite_ref-uprising_50-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uprising-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Monuments and government buildings were blown up by special German troops known as <i>Verbrennungs- und Vernichtungskommando</i> ("Burning and Destruction Detachments").<sup id="cite_ref-uprising_50-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uprising-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> About 85% of the city had been destroyed, including the historic Old Town and the Royal Castle.<sup id="cite_ref-warsawuprising_com_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-warsawuprising_com-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 17 January 1945&#160;– after the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Vistula%E2%80%93Oder_Offensive" title="Vistula–Oder Offensive">Vistula–Oder Offensive</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">Red Army</a>&#160;– Soviet troops and Polish troops of the <a href="/wiki/First_Polish_Army_(1944-1945)" class="mw-redirect" title="First Polish Army (1944-1945)">First Polish Army</a> entered the ruins of Warsaw, and liberated Warsaw's suburbs from German occupation.<sup id="cite_ref-Adamczyk_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Adamczyk-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> The city was swiftly taken by the Soviet Army, which rapidly advanced towards <a href="/wiki/%C5%81%C3%B3d%C5%BA" title="Łódź">Łódź</a>, as German forces regrouped at a more westward position.
</p>
<h3><span id="1945.E2.80.931989:_Warsaw_during_the_People.27s_Republic"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1945–1989:_Warsaw_during_the_People's_Republic">1945–1989: Warsaw during the People's Republic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 1945–1989: Warsaw during the People&#039;s Republic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1945, after the bombings, revolts, fighting, and demolition had ended, most of Warsaw lay in ruins.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A_Kult%C3%BAra_%C3%A9s_Tudom%C3%A1ny_Palot%C3%A1ja._Fortepan_59944.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/A_Kult%C3%BAra_%C3%A9s_Tudom%C3%A1ny_Palot%C3%A1ja._Fortepan_59944.jpg/220px-A_Kult%C3%BAra_%C3%A9s_Tudom%C3%A1ny_Palot%C3%A1ja._Fortepan_59944.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="216" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/A_Kult%C3%BAra_%C3%A9s_Tudom%C3%A1ny_Palot%C3%A1ja._Fortepan_59944.jpg/330px-A_Kult%C3%BAra_%C3%A9s_Tudom%C3%A1ny_Palot%C3%A1ja._Fortepan_59944.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/A_Kult%C3%BAra_%C3%A9s_Tudom%C3%A1ny_Palot%C3%A1ja._Fortepan_59944.jpg/440px-A_Kult%C3%BAra_%C3%A9s_Tudom%C3%A1ny_Palot%C3%A1ja._Fortepan_59944.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6657" data-file-height="6545" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A_Kult%C3%BAra_%C3%A9s_Tudom%C3%A1ny_Palot%C3%A1ja._Fortepan_59944.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A tourist standing beside the iconic <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Culture_and_Science" title="Palace of Culture and Science">Palace of Culture and Science</a>, 1965</div></div></div>
<p>After World War II, the "Bricks for Warsaw" campaign was initiated, and large <a href="/wiki/Prefabrication" title="Prefabrication">prefabricated</a> <a href="/wiki/Public_housing" title="Public housing">housing projects</a> were erected in Warsaw to address the housing shortage, along with other typical buildings of an <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Eastern Bloc</a> city, such as the <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Culture_and_Science,_Warsaw" class="mw-redirect" title="Palace of Culture and Science, Warsaw">Palace of Culture and Science</a>, a gift from the Soviet Union. The city resumed its role as the capital of Poland and the country's centre of political and economic life. Many of the historic streets, buildings, and churches were restored to their original form. In 1980, Warsaw's historic Old Town was inscribed onto <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>'s <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage</a> list.<sup id="cite_ref-unesco_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unesco-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II" title="Pope John Paul II">John Paul II</a>'s visits to his native country in 1979 and 1983 brought support to the budding <a href="/wiki/Solidarity_(Polish_trade_union)" title="Solidarity (Polish trade union)">"Solidarity" movement</a> and encouraged the growing <a href="/wiki/Anti-communism" title="Anti-communism">anti-communist</a> fervor there.<sup id="cite_ref-destination_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-destination-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> In 1979, less than a year after becoming pope, John Paul celebrated Mass in <a href="/wiki/Pi%C5%82sudski_Square" title="Piłsudski Square">Victory Square</a> in Warsaw and ended his sermon with a call to "renew the face" of Poland: <i>Let Thy Spirit descend! Let Thy Spirit descend and renew the face of the land! This land!</i><sup id="cite_ref-destination_55-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-destination-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> These words were very meaningful for the Polish citizens who understood them as the incentive for liberal-democratic reforms.<sup id="cite_ref-destination_55-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-destination-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Recent_times:_1989.E2.80.93present"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Recent_times:_1989–present">Recent times: 1989–present</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Recent times: 1989–present">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1995, the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Metro" title="Warsaw Metro">Warsaw Metro</a> opened with a single line. A second line was opened in March 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> With the entry of Poland into the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> in 2004, Warsaw is currently experiencing the largest economic boom of its history.<sup id="cite_ref-polandtrade_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-polandtrade-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> The opening fixture of <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012" title="UEFA Euro 2012">UEFA Euro 2012</a> took place in Warsaw, a game in which Poland drew 1–1 with Greece.<sup id="cite_ref-poland2012_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-poland2012-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Warsaw was the host city for the <a href="/wiki/2013_United_Nations_Climate_Change_Conference" title="2013 United Nations Climate Change Conference">2013 United Nations Climate Change Conference</a> and for the <a href="/wiki/2016_Warsaw_summit" title="2016 Warsaw summit">2016 NATO Summit</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Location_and_topography">Location and topography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Location and topography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:WarsawFromTheISS.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/WarsawFromTheISS.jpg/220px-WarsawFromTheISS.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/WarsawFromTheISS.jpg/330px-WarsawFromTheISS.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/WarsawFromTheISS.jpg/440px-WarsawFromTheISS.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="681" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:WarsawFromTheISS.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Warsaw, seen from the <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">International Space Station</a></div></div></div>
<p>Warsaw lies in east-central Poland about 300&#160;km (190&#160;mi) from the <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Mountains" title="Carpathian Mountains">Carpathian Mountains</a> and about 260&#160;km (160&#160;mi) from the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic Sea</a>, 523&#160;km (325&#160;mi) east of Berlin, Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> The city straddles the <a href="/wiki/Vistula" title="Vistula">Vistula</a> River. It is located in the heartland of the <a href="/wiki/Masovian_Plain" class="mw-redirect" title="Masovian Plain">Masovian Plain</a>, and its average elevation is 100 metres (330&#160;ft) above sea level. The highest point on the left side of the city lies at a height of 115.7 metres (379.6&#160;ft) ("Redutowa" bus depot, district of Wola), on the right side&#160;– 122.1 metres (400.6&#160;ft) ("Groszówka" estate, district of Wesoła, by the eastern border). The lowest point lies at a height 75.6 metres (248.0&#160;ft) (at the right bank of the Vistula, by the eastern border of Warsaw). There are some hills (mostly artificial) located within the confines of the city&#160;– e.g. Warsaw Uprising Hill (121 metres (397.0&#160;ft)) and Szczęśliwice hill (138 metres (452.8&#160;ft)&#160;– the highest point of Warsaw in general).
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Plac_Grzybowski_noc%C4%85.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Plac_Grzybowski_noc%C4%85.jpg/220px-Plac_Grzybowski_noc%C4%85.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Plac_Grzybowski_noc%C4%85.jpg/330px-Plac_Grzybowski_noc%C4%85.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Plac_Grzybowski_noc%C4%85.jpg/440px-Plac_Grzybowski_noc%C4%85.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3300" data-file-height="2200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Plac_Grzybowski_noc%C4%85.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View of <a href="/wiki/Grzybowski_Square" title="Grzybowski Square">Grzybowski Square</a> in the <a href="/wiki/%C5%9Ar%C3%B3dmie%C5%9Bcie,_Warsaw" title="Śródmieście, Warsaw">central district of Warsaw</a>. The city is located on the mostly flat <a href="/wiki/Masovian_Plain" class="mw-redirect" title="Masovian Plain">Masovian Plain</a>, but the city centre is at a higher elevation than the suburbs.</div></div></div>
<p>Warsaw is located on two main geomorphologic formations: the plain moraine plateau and the Vistula Valley with its asymmetrical pattern of different terraces. The Vistula River is the specific axis of Warsaw, which divides the city into two parts, left and right. The left one is situated both on the <a href="/wiki/Moraine" title="Moraine">moraine</a> plateau (10 to 25&#160;m (32.8 to 82.0&#160;ft) above Vistula level) and on the Vistula terraces (max. 6.5&#160;m (21.3&#160;ft) above Vistula level). The significant element of the relief, in this part of Warsaw, is the edge of moraine plateau called Warsaw Escarpment. It is 20 to 25&#160;m (65.6 to 82.0&#160;ft) high in the Old Town and Central district and about 10&#160;m (32.8&#160;ft) in the north and south of Warsaw. It goes through the city and plays an important role as a landmark.
</p><p>The plain moraine plateau has only a few natural and artificial ponds and also groups of <a href="/wiki/Clay_pit" title="Clay pit">clay pits</a>. The pattern of the Vistula terraces is asymmetrical. The left side consists mainly of two levels: the highest one contains former flooded terraces and the lowest one the flood plain terrace. The contemporary flooded terrace still has visible valleys and ground <a href="/wiki/Depression_(geology)" title="Depression (geology)">depressions</a> with water systems coming from the old Vistula&#160;– riverbed. They consist of still quite natural streams and lakes as well as the pattern of drainage ditches. The right side of Warsaw has a different pattern of geomorphological forms. There are several levels of the Vistula plain terraces (flooded as well as formerly flooded), and only a small part is a not so visible moraine escarpment. <a href="/wiki/Aeolian_processes" title="Aeolian processes">Aeolian</a> sand with a number of dunes parted by <a href="/wiki/Peat" title="Peat">peat</a> swamps or small ponds cover the highest terrace. These are mainly forested areas (<a href="/wiki/Temperate_coniferous_forest" title="Temperate coniferous forest">pine forest</a>).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Officially, Warsaw experiences an <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic climate</a>, denoted by <i>Cfb</i> by <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen's original classification</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> But the city being in the midst of Siberian air mass and far from the coast has clear continental influences (<i>Dfb</i>), defined as such with old data.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-noaa_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-noaa-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> And, by the Köppen-Geiger climate classification measure, Warsaw is currently defined as having a <a href="/wiki/Humid_continental_climate" title="Humid continental climate">humid continental climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a> <i>Dfb</i>), with long cold winters and short warm summers, though the <a href="/wiki/Urban_heat_island" title="Urban heat island">urban heat island</a> effect does make Warsaw's winters slightly less severe than in the surrounding rural areas.<sup id="cite_ref-PeelFinlayson2007_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PeelFinlayson2007-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BłażejczykBaranowski2015_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BłażejczykBaranowski2015-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> However, by classification of the <a href="/wiki/Wincenty_Oko%C5%82owicz" title="Wincenty Okołowicz">Wincenty Okołowicz</a>, it has a <a href="/wiki/Temperate_climate" title="Temperate climate">warm-temperate climate</a> in the center of <a href="/wiki/Continental_Europe" title="Continental Europe">continental Europe</a> with the "fusion" of different features.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> The city has cold, snowy, cloudy winters and warm, sunny, stormy summers. Spring and autumn can be unpredictable, highly prone to sudden weather changes; however, temperatures are usually mild and with low humidity, especially around May and September.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_62-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> The average temperature ranges between −1.8&#160;°C (29&#160;°F) in January and 19.2&#160;°C (66.6&#160;°F) in July. The mean year temperature is 8.5&#160;°C (47.3&#160;°F). Temperatures may often reach 30&#160;°C (86&#160;°F) in the summer, although the effects of hot weather are usually offset by relatively low dew points and large diurnal temperature differences. Warsaw is Europe's sixth driest major city (third in <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a>), with yearly rainfall averaging 529 millimetres (20.8&#160;in), the wettest month being July.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cityscape">Cityscape</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Cityscape">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Warsaw's mixture of architectural styles reflects the turbulent <a href="/wiki/History_of_Warsaw" title="History of Warsaw">history of the city</a> and country. During the Second World War, Warsaw was razed to the ground by <a href="/wiki/Bombing_of_Warsaw_in_World_War_II" title="Bombing of Warsaw in World War II">bombing raids</a> and <a href="/wiki/Planned_destruction_of_Warsaw" class="mw-redirect" title="Planned destruction of Warsaw">planned destruction</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-uprising_50-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uprising-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> After liberation, rebuilding began as in other cities of the communist-ruled <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Republic_of_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="People&#39;s Republic of Poland">People's Republic of Poland</a>. Most of the historical buildings were thoroughly reconstructed. However, some of the buildings from the 19th century that had been preserved in reasonably reconstructible form were nonetheless eradicated in the 1950s and 1960s (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Leopold_Stanis%C5%82aw_Kronenberg" title="Leopold Stanisław Kronenberg">Kronenberg Palace</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Mass residential blocks were erected, with basic design typical of <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc" title="Eastern Bloc">Eastern Bloc</a> countries.
</p><p>Public spaces attract heavy investment, so that the city has gained entirely new squares, parks and monuments. Warsaw's current urban landscape is one of modern and contemporary architecture.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin:0 auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:1308px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a href="/wiki/File:Panorama_Warszawy_by_Night_SS.jpg" class="image" title="Panorama of Warsaw by night"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Panorama_Warszawy_by_Night_SS.jpg/1300px-Panorama_Warszawy_by_Night_SS.jpg" decoding="async" width="1300" height="133" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Panorama_Warszawy_by_Night_SS.jpg/1950px-Panorama_Warszawy_by_Night_SS.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Panorama_Warszawy_by_Night_SS.jpg/2600px-Panorama_Warszawy_by_Night_SS.jpg 2x" data-file-width="21375" data-file-height="2189" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:center"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Panorama_Warszawy_by_Night_SS.jpg" title="File:Panorama Warszawy by Night SS.jpg"> </a></div>Panorama of Warsaw by night</div></div></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Architecture">Architecture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Architecture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_Warsaw" title="Architecture of Warsaw">Architecture of Warsaw</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Warszawa_pa%C5%82ac_Jab%C5%82onowskich_2009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Warszawa_pa%C5%82ac_Jab%C5%82onowskich_2009.jpg/300px-Warszawa_pa%C5%82ac_Jab%C5%82onowskich_2009.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Warszawa_pa%C5%82ac_Jab%C5%82onowskich_2009.jpg/450px-Warszawa_pa%C5%82ac_Jab%C5%82onowskich_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Warszawa_pa%C5%82ac_Jab%C5%82onowskich_2009.jpg/600px-Warszawa_pa%C5%82ac_Jab%C5%82onowskich_2009.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6014" data-file-height="2898" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Warszawa_pa%C5%82ac_Jab%C5%82onowskich_2009.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Jab%C5%82onowski_Palace" title="Jabłonowski Palace">Jabłonowski Palace</a>, an example of <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_Revival_architecture" title="Renaissance Revival architecture">Renaissance Revival architecture</a></div></div></div>
<p>Warsaw's <a href="/wiki/Palace" title="Palace">palaces</a>, churches and mansions display a richness of color and architectural details. Buildings are representatives of nearly every European architectural style and <a href="/wiki/List_of_time_periods" title="List of time periods">historical period</a>. The city has wonderful examples of architecture from the <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">Gothic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baroque" title="Baroque">Baroque</a> and <a href="/wiki/Neoclassical_architecture" title="Neoclassical architecture">neoclassical</a> periods, all of which are located within easy walking distance of the town centre.
</p><p>Gothic architecture is represented in the majestic churches but also at the <a href="/wiki/Middle_class" title="Middle class">burgher</a> houses and fortifications. The most significant buildings are <a href="/wiki/St._John%27s_Cathedral,_Warsaw" class="mw-redirect" title="St. John&#39;s Cathedral, Warsaw">St. John's Cathedral</a> (14th century), a typical example of the so-called <a href="/wiki/Masovia" class="mw-redirect" title="Masovia">Masovian</a> Gothic style; <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Visitation_of_the_Blessed_Virgin_Mary,_Warsaw" title="Church of the Visitation of the Blessed Virgin Mary, Warsaw">St. Mary's Church</a> (1411), a <a href="/wiki/Townhouse" title="Townhouse">town house</a> of Burbach family (14th century);<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Gunpowder Tower (after 1379); and the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Castle,_Warsaw" title="Royal Castle, Warsaw">Royal Castle</a> <i>Curia Maior</i> (1407–1410). The most notable examples of <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_architecture" title="Renaissance architecture">Renaissance architecture</a> in the city are the house of the Baryczko merchant family (1562), a building called "The Negro" (early 17th century), and Salwator tenement (1632). The most interesting examples of <a href="/wiki/Mannerism" title="Mannerism">Mannerist</a> architecture are the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Castle,_Warsaw" title="Royal Castle, Warsaw">Royal Castle</a> (1596–1619) and the <a href="/wiki/Jesuit_Church,_Warsaw" title="Jesuit Church, Warsaw">Jesuit Church</a> (1609–1626) at Old Town. Among the first structures of the early Baroque, the most important are <a href="/wiki/St._Hyacinth%27s_Church,_Warsaw" title="St. Hyacinth&#39;s Church, Warsaw">St. Hyacinth's Church</a> (1603–1639) and <a href="/wiki/Sigismund%27s_Column" title="Sigismund&#39;s Column">Sigismund's Column</a> (1644).
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hotel_Bristol,_Warszawa.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Hotel_Bristol%2C_Warszawa.jpg/170px-Hotel_Bristol%2C_Warszawa.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Hotel_Bristol%2C_Warszawa.jpg/255px-Hotel_Bristol%2C_Warszawa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Hotel_Bristol%2C_Warszawa.jpg/340px-Hotel_Bristol%2C_Warszawa.jpg 2x" data-file-width="667" data-file-height="1000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hotel_Bristol,_Warszawa.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Hotel_Bristol,_Warsaw" title="Hotel Bristol, Warsaw">Hotel Bristol</a> is a unique example of Warsaw's architectural heritage.</div></div></div>
<p>Building activity occurred in numerous noble palaces and churches during the later decades of the 17th century. Some of the best examples of this architecture are <a href="/wiki/Krasi%C5%84ski_Palace" title="Krasiński Palace">Krasiński Palace</a> (1677–1683), <a href="/wiki/Wilan%C3%B3w_Palace" title="Wilanów Palace">Wilanów Palace</a> (1677–1696) and <a href="/wiki/St._Kazimierz_Church" title="St. Kazimierz Church">St. Kazimierz Church</a> (1688–1692). The most impressive examples of <a href="/wiki/Rococo" title="Rococo">rococo</a> architecture are <a href="/wiki/Czapski_Palace" title="Czapski Palace">Czapski Palace</a> (1712–1721), <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_the_Four_Winds" title="Palace of the Four Winds">Palace of the Four Winds</a> (1730s) and <a href="/wiki/Visitationist_Church" title="Visitationist Church">Visitationist Church</a> (façade 1728–1761). The neoclassical architecture in Warsaw can be described by the simplicity of the geometrical forms teamed with a great inspiration from the Roman period. Some of the best examples of the neoclassical style are the <a href="/wiki/%C5%81azienki_Palace" class="mw-redirect" title="Łazienki Palace">Palace on the Water</a> (rebuilt 1775–1795), <a href="/wiki/Kr%C3%B3likarnia" title="Królikarnia">Królikarnia</a> (1782–1786), <a href="/wiki/Carmelite_Church,_Warsaw" title="Carmelite Church, Warsaw">Carmelite Church</a> (façade 1761–1783) and Evangelical <a href="/wiki/Holy_Trinity_Church,_Warsaw" title="Holy Trinity Church, Warsaw">Holy Trinity Church</a> (1777–1782). The economic growth during the first years of <a href="/wiki/Congress_Poland" title="Congress Poland">Congress Poland</a> caused a rapid rise of architecture. The Neoclassical revival affected all aspects of architecture; the most notable examples are the <a href="/wiki/Great_Theatre,_Warsaw" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Theatre, Warsaw">Great Theater</a> (1825–1833) and buildings located at <a href="/wiki/Plac_Bankowy,_Warsaw" class="mw-redirect" title="Plac Bankowy, Warsaw">Bank Square</a> (1825–1828).
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:6_Warszawa_149.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/6_Warszawa_149.jpg/170px-6_Warszawa_149.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="239" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/6_Warszawa_149.jpg/255px-6_Warszawa_149.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/6_Warszawa_149.jpg/340px-6_Warszawa_149.jpg 2x" data-file-width="533" data-file-height="750" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:6_Warszawa_149.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Warsaw_University_of_Technology" title="Warsaw University of Technology">Warsaw University of Technology</a> building courtyard</div></div></div>
<p>Exceptional examples of the <a href="/wiki/Bourgeoisie" title="Bourgeoisie">bourgeois</a> architecture of the later periods were not restored by the <a href="/wiki/Communism" title="Communism">communist</a> authorities after the war (like the previously mentioned Kronenberg Palace and insurance company Rosja building) or they were rebuilt in socialist realism style (like <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Philharmonic_Orchestra" class="mw-redirect" title="Warsaw Philharmonic Orchestra">Warsaw Philharmony</a> edifice originally inspired by <a href="/wiki/Palais_Garnier" title="Palais Garnier">Palais Garnier</a> in Paris). Despite that, the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_University_of_Technology" title="Warsaw University of Technology">Warsaw University of Technology</a> building (1899–1902)<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> is the most interesting of the late 19th-century architecture. Some 19th-century buildings in the Praga district (the Vistula's right bank) have been restored although many have been poorly maintained. Warsaw's municipal government authorities have decided to rebuild the <a href="/wiki/Saxon_Palace" title="Saxon Palace">Saxon Palace</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Br%C3%BChl_Palace,_Warsaw" title="Brühl Palace, Warsaw">Brühl Palace</a>, the most distinctive buildings in prewar Warsaw.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Notable examples of post-war architecture include the <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Culture_and_Science,_Warsaw" class="mw-redirect" title="Palace of Culture and Science, Warsaw">Palace of Culture and Science</a> (1952–1955), a <a href="/wiki/Socialist_realism" title="Socialist realism">soc-realist</a> skyscraper located in the city centre, and the <a href="/wiki/Plac_Konstytucji" title="Plac Konstytucji">Constitution Square</a> with its monumental <a href="/wiki/Socialist_realism" title="Socialist realism">socialist realism</a> architecture (MDM estate).<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Contemporary_architecture" title="Contemporary architecture">Contemporary architecture</a> in Warsaw is represented by the Metropolitan Office Building at <a href="/wiki/Pi%C5%82sudski_Square" title="Piłsudski Square">Pilsudski Square</a> by <a href="/wiki/Norman_Foster_(architect)" class="mw-redirect" title="Norman Foster (architect)">Norman Foster</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Metropolitan_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Metropolitan-83">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_University_Library" title="Warsaw University Library">Warsaw University Library</a> (BUW) by Marek Budzyński and Zbigniew Badowski, featuring a garden on its roof and view of the Vistula River, <a href="/wiki/Rondo_1" title="Rondo 1">Rondo 1</a> office building by <a href="/wiki/Skidmore,_Owings_%26_Merrill" title="Skidmore, Owings &amp; Merrill">Skidmore, Owings &amp; Merrill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_the_History_of_Polish_Jews" class="mw-redirect" title="Museum of the History of Polish Jews">Museum of the History of Polish Jews</a> by <a href="/wiki/Rainer_Mahlam%C3%A4ki" title="Rainer Mahlamäki">Rainer Mahlamäki</a> and <a href="/wiki/Z%C5%82ote_Tarasy" title="Złote Tarasy">Golden Terraces</a>, consisting of seven overlapping domes retail and business centre.
</p><p>Together with Frankfurt, London, Paris and Rotterdam, Warsaw is one of the cities with the highest number of skyscrapers in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-scraper_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scraper-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Warsaw is ranked as 79th in the <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_with_the_most_skyscrapers" title="List of cities with the most skyscrapers">list of cities with the most skyscrapers</a> around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
