<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Landmarks">Landmarks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Landmarks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tourist_attractions_in_Warsaw" title="Tourist attractions in Warsaw">Tourist attractions in Warsaw</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Warszawa,_Rynek_Starego_Miasta_36-28_20170518_002.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Warszawa%2C_Rynek_Starego_Miasta_36-28_20170518_002.jpg/220px-Warszawa%2C_Rynek_Starego_Miasta_36-28_20170518_002.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Warszawa%2C_Rynek_Starego_Miasta_36-28_20170518_002.jpg/330px-Warszawa%2C_Rynek_Starego_Miasta_36-28_20170518_002.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Warszawa%2C_Rynek_Starego_Miasta_36-28_20170518_002.jpg/440px-Warszawa%2C_Rynek_Starego_Miasta_36-28_20170518_002.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5995" data-file-height="4002" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Warszawa,_Rynek_Starego_Miasta_36-28_20170518_002.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Old_Town_Market_Place,_Warsaw" title="Old Town Market Place, Warsaw">Main Market Square</a> in <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Old_Town" title="Warsaw Old Town">Old Town</a>, a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCO World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage Site</a></div></div></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886046874">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .mobile-float-reset{float:none!important;width:100%!important}}.mw-parser-output .stack-container{box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .stack-clear-left{float:left;clear:left}.mw-parser-output .stack-clear-right{float:right;clear:right}.mw-parser-output .stack-left{float:left}.mw-parser-output .stack-right{float:right}.mw-parser-output .stack-object{margin:1px;overflow:hidden}</style><div class="mw-stack stack-container stack-clear-right mobile-float-reset"><div class="stack-object">
<table style="float:right;">
<tbody><tr>
<td><div class="mw-collapsible mw-collapsed" style="box-sizing:border-box;width:100%;font-size:95%;padding:4px;border:none;"><div style="font-size:100%;line-height:1.6;font-weight:bold;background:transparent;text-align:center;;width: 285px; background: #B5B5B5;">Map of Warsaw Old Town</div><div class="mw-collapsible-content" style="background:transparent;text-align:left;;">
<div class="center"><div class="thumb tnone"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Old_Town_in_Warsaw_map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Old_Town_in_Warsaw_map.png/280px-Old_Town_in_Warsaw_map.png" decoding="async" width="280" height="309" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Old_Town_in_Warsaw_map.png/420px-Old_Town_in_Warsaw_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Old_Town_in_Warsaw_map.png/560px-Old_Town_in_Warsaw_map.png 2x" data-file-width="1497" data-file-height="1650" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Old_Town_in_Warsaw_map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><div><ol><li>Stone stairs</li><li><a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Warsaw" title="Museum of Warsaw">Museum of Warsaw</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Barbican" title="Warsaw Barbican">Barbican</a></li><li>Defensive walls</li><li>Salwator tenement</li><li>Museum of Leather Crafts</li><li>St. Anne's tenement</li><li>Fukier tenement</li><li>Museum of Literature</li><li>Museum of Artistic and Precision Crafts</li><li><a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Visitation_of_the_Blessed_Virgin_Mary,_Warsaw" title="Church of the Visitation of the Blessed Virgin Mary, Warsaw">St. Mary's Church</a></li><li>Gothic Bridge</li><li>Pelican house</li><li><a href="/wiki/St._John%27s_Cathedral,_Warsaw" class="mw-redirect" title="St. John&#39;s Cathedral, Warsaw">St. John's Cathedral</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Jesuit_Church,_Warsaw" title="Jesuit Church, Warsaw">Jesuit Church</a></li><li>Canonicity</li><li><a href="/wiki/Royal_Castle,_Warsaw" title="Royal Castle, Warsaw">Royal Castle</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Copper-Roof_Palace" title="Copper-Roof Palace">Copper-Roof Palace</a></li><li>East&#160;– West Route tunnel</li><li>Dung Hill</li><li>Warsaw Mermaid statue</li><li><a href="/wiki/Sigismund%27s_Column" title="Sigismund&#39;s Column">Sigismund's Column</a></li></ol></div></div></div></div></div></div></div>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
</div></div>
<p>Although contemporary Warsaw is a fairly young city compared to other European capitals, it has numerous <a href="/wiki/Tourist_attraction" title="Tourist attraction">tourist attractions</a> and architectural monuments dating back centuries. Apart from the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Old_Town" title="Warsaw Old Town">Warsaw Old Town</a> quarter, reconstructed after World War II, each borough has something to offer. Among the most notable landmarks of the Old Town are the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Castle,_Warsaw" title="Royal Castle, Warsaw">Royal Castle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sigismund%27s_Column" title="Sigismund&#39;s Column">Sigismund's Column</a>, <a href="/wiki/Old_Town_Market_Place,_Warsaw" title="Old Town Market Place, Warsaw">Market Square</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Barbican" title="Warsaw Barbican">Barbican</a>.
</p><p>Further south is the so-called <a href="/wiki/Royal_Route,_Warsaw" title="Royal Route, Warsaw">Royal Route</a>, with many historical churches, <a href="/wiki/Baroque_architecture" title="Baroque architecture">Baroque</a> and <a href="/wiki/Classicism" title="Classicism">Classicist</a> palaces, most notably the <a href="/wiki/Presidential_Palace,_Warsaw" title="Presidential Palace, Warsaw">Presidential Palace</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Warsaw" title="University of Warsaw">University of Warsaw</a> campus. The former royal residence of King <a href="/wiki/John_III_Sobieski" title="John III Sobieski">John III Sobieski</a> at <a href="/wiki/Wilan%C3%B3w_Palace" title="Wilanów Palace">Wilanów</a> is notable for its Baroque architecture and eloquent palatial garden.<sup id="cite_ref-wilanow-palac_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wilanow-palac-85">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Warsaw's oldest public park, the <a href="/wiki/Saxon_Garden" title="Saxon Garden">Saxon Garden</a>, is located within 10 minutes' walk from the Old Town. It was opened in 1727.<sup id="cite_ref-Fragmenta_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fragmenta-86">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> Warsaw's largest park is the <a href="/wiki/%C5%81azienki_Park" title="Łazienki Park">Łazienki Park</a>, also called the "Royal Baths Park", established in the 17th century and given its current classical shape in the late 18th century.<sup id="cite_ref-lazienki_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lazienki-87">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> It is located further south, on the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Route,_Warsaw" title="Royal Route, Warsaw">Royal Route</a>, about 3&#160;km (1.9&#160;mi) from the Warsaw Old Town.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Pow%C4%85zki_Cemetery" title="Powązki Cemetery">Powązki Cemetery</a> is one of the oldest cemeteries in Europe,<sup id="cite_ref-rsi_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rsi-88">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> featuring of sculptures, some of them by the most renowned Polish artists of the 19th and 20th centuries. Since it serves the <a href="/wiki/Religion" title="Religion">religious communities</a> of Warsaw such as Catholics, Jews, Orthodox Christians, Muslims or Protestants, it is often called a <a href="/wiki/List_of_necropoleis" title="List of necropoleis">necropolis</a>. Nearby is the <a href="/wiki/Okopowa_Street_Jewish_Cemetery" class="mw-redirect" title="Okopowa Street Jewish Cemetery">Okopowa Street Jewish Cemetery</a>, one of the largest Jewish cemeteries in Europe.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Warszawa,_ul._Nowy_%C5%9Awiat_49,_51_20170516_001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Warszawa%2C_ul._Nowy_%C5%9Awiat_49%2C_51_20170516_001.jpg/220px-Warszawa%2C_ul._Nowy_%C5%9Awiat_49%2C_51_20170516_001.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Warszawa%2C_ul._Nowy_%C5%9Awiat_49%2C_51_20170516_001.jpg/330px-Warszawa%2C_ul._Nowy_%C5%9Awiat_49%2C_51_20170516_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Warszawa%2C_ul._Nowy_%C5%9Awiat_49%2C_51_20170516_001.jpg/440px-Warszawa%2C_ul._Nowy_%C5%9Awiat_49%2C_51_20170516_001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5996" data-file-height="4003" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Warszawa,_ul._Nowy_%C5%9Awiat_49,_51_20170516_001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/New_World_Street" class="mw-redirect" title="New World Street">New World Street</a>, one of the main shopping promenades in Warsaw</div></div></div>
<p>In many places in the city the <a href="/wiki/Secular_Jewish_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Secular Jewish culture">Jewish culture</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Poland" title="History of the Jews in Poland">history</a> resonates down through time.<sup id="cite_ref-judaica_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-judaica-89">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> Among them the most notable are the <a href="/wiki/Jewish_Theatre,_Warsaw" title="Jewish Theatre, Warsaw">Jewish theater</a>, the <a href="/wiki/No%C5%BCyk_Synagogue" title="Nożyk Synagogue">Nożyk Synagogue</a>, <a href="/wiki/Janusz_Korczak" title="Janusz Korczak">Janusz Korczak</a>'s Orphanage and the picturesque Próżna Street.<sup id="cite_ref-judaica_89-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-judaica-89">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> The tragic pages of Warsaw's history are commemorated in places such as the <a href="/wiki/Monument_to_the_Ghetto_Heroes" title="Monument to the Ghetto Heroes">Monument to the Ghetto Heroes</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Umschlagplatz_(Warsaw_Ghetto)" class="mw-redirect" title="Umschlagplatz (Warsaw Ghetto)">Umschlagplatz</a>, fragments of the Ghetto wall on Sienna Street and a mound in memory of the <a href="/wiki/Jewish_Combat_Organization" title="Jewish Combat Organization">Jewish Combat Organization</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-judaica_89-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-judaica-89">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There are also many places commemorating the heroic history of Warsaw.<sup id="cite_ref-heroic_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heroic-90">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pawiak" class="mw-redirect" title="Pawiak">Pawiak</a>, an infamous German <a href="/wiki/Gestapo" title="Gestapo">Gestapo</a> prison now occupied by a <a href="/wiki/Mausoleum" title="Mausoleum">Mausoleum</a> of Memory of <a href="/wiki/Martyr" title="Martyr">Martyrdom</a> and the museum, is only the beginning of a walk in the traces of Heroic City.<sup id="cite_ref-heroic_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heroic-90">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Citadel" title="Warsaw Citadel">Warsaw Citadel</a>, an impressive 19th-century fortification built after the defeat of the <a href="/wiki/November_uprising" class="mw-redirect" title="November uprising">November uprising</a>, was a place of martyrdom for the Poles.<sup id="cite_ref-heroic_90-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heroic-90">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> Another important monument, the statue of <a href="/wiki/Ma%C5%82y_Powstaniec" title="Mały Powstaniec">Little Insurrectionist</a> located at the ramparts of the Old Town, commemorates the children who served as messengers and frontline troops in the Warsaw Uprising, while the impressive <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Uprising_Monument" title="Warsaw Uprising Monument">Warsaw Uprising Monument</a> by Wincenty Kućma was erected in memory of the largest insurrection of World War II.<sup id="cite_ref-heroic_90-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heroic-90">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Montagu_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Montagu-91">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In Warsaw there are many places connected with the life and work of <a href="/wiki/Fr%C3%A9d%C3%A9ric_Chopin" title="Frédéric Chopin">Frédéric Chopin</a> who was born near the city in <a href="/wiki/%C5%BBelazowa_Wola" title="Żelazowa Wola">Żelazowa Wola</a>. The heart of the Polish composer is sealed inside Warsaw's <a href="/wiki/Holy_Cross_Church,_Warsaw" title="Holy Cross Church, Warsaw">Holy Cross Church</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Holy_Cross_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Holy_Cross-92">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> During the summer time the <a href="/wiki/Chopin_Statue,_Warsaw" title="Chopin Statue, Warsaw">Chopin Statue</a> in Łazienki Park is a place where pianists give concerts to the park audience.<sup id="cite_ref-Chopin_Monument_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chopin_Monument-93">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Also many references to <a href="/wiki/Marie_Curie" title="Marie Curie">Marie Curie</a>, her work and her family can be found in Warsaw; Curie's birthplace at the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_New_Town" title="Warsaw New Town">Warsaw New Town</a>, the working places where she did her first scientific works<sup id="cite_ref-aip1_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aip1-94">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Curie_Institute_(Warsaw)" class="mw-redirect" title="Curie Institute (Warsaw)">Radium Institute</a> at Wawelska Street for the research and the treatment of which she founded in 1925.<sup id="cite_ref-aip2_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aip2-95">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

		</div></li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 182px"><div style="width: 182px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 180px;"><div style="margin:0px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Barbakan_w_Warszawie_-_03.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Barbakan_w_Warszawie_-_03.jpg/270px-Barbakan_w_Warszawie_-_03.jpg" decoding="async" width="180" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Barbakan_w_Warszawie_-_03.jpg/405px-Barbakan_w_Warszawie_-_03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Barbakan_w_Warszawie_-_03.jpg/540px-Barbakan_w_Warszawie_-_03.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3417" data-file-height="2278" /></a></div></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">

</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
</ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Flora_and_fauna">Flora and fauna</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Flora and fauna">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Green space covers almost a quarter of the area of Warsaw,<sup id="cite_ref-warsaw_tour_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-warsaw_tour-96">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> including a broad range from small neighborhood parks, green spaces along streets and in courtyards, to avenues of trees and large historic parks, nature conservation areas and the urban forests at the fringe of the city.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Palace_on_the_Water,_%C5%81azienki_Park,_Warsaw.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Palace_on_the_Water%2C_%C5%81azienki_Park%2C_Warsaw.jpg/220px-Palace_on_the_Water%2C_%C5%81azienki_Park%2C_Warsaw.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Palace_on_the_Water%2C_%C5%81azienki_Park%2C_Warsaw.jpg/330px-Palace_on_the_Water%2C_%C5%81azienki_Park%2C_Warsaw.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Palace_on_the_Water%2C_%C5%81azienki_Park%2C_Warsaw.jpg/440px-Palace_on_the_Water%2C_%C5%81azienki_Park%2C_Warsaw.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1509" data-file-height="1134" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Palace_on_the_Water,_%C5%81azienki_Park,_Warsaw.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/%C5%81azienki_Palace" class="mw-redirect" title="Łazienki Palace">Łazienki Palace</a>, also referred to as the <i>Palace on the Isle</i></div></div></div>
<p>There are as many as 82 parks in the city which cover 8% of its area.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> The oldest ones, once parts of representative palaces, are <a href="/wiki/Saxon_Garden" title="Saxon Garden">Saxon Garden</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Krasi%C5%84ski_Palace" title="Krasiński Palace">Krasiński Palace</a> Garden, <a href="/wiki/%C5%81azienki_Park" title="Łazienki Park">Łazienki Park</a> (Royal Baths Park), <a href="/wiki/Wilan%C3%B3w_Palace" title="Wilanów Palace">Wilanów Palace</a> Park and <a href="/wiki/Kr%C3%B3likarnia" title="Królikarnia">Królikarnia</a> Palace Park (<i>See also: <a href="#Warsaw_in_art_and_literature">Greenery in the city</a></i>).
</p><p>The Saxon Garden, covering an area of 15.5 ha, was formally a royal garden. There are over 100 different species of trees and the avenues are a place to sit and relax. At the east end of the park, the <a href="/wiki/Tomb_of_the_Unknown_Soldier,_Warsaw" class="mw-redirect" title="Tomb of the Unknown Soldier, Warsaw">Tomb of the Unknown Soldier</a> is situated. In the 19th century the Krasiński Palace Garden was remodelled by Franciszek Szanior. Within the central area of the park one can still find old trees dating from that period: <a href="/wiki/Ginkgo_biloba" title="Ginkgo biloba">maidenhair tree</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juglans_nigra" title="Juglans nigra">black walnut</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corylus_colurna" title="Corylus colurna">Turkish hazel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pterocarya_fraxinifolia" title="Pterocarya fraxinifolia">Caucasian wingnut</a> trees. With its benches, flower carpets, a pond with ducks on and a playground for kids, the Krasiński Palace Garden is a popular strolling destination for the Varsovians. The Monument of the Warsaw Ghetto Uprising is also situated here. Łazienki Park covers an area of 76 ha. The unique character and history of the park is reflected in its <a href="/wiki/Landscape_architecture" title="Landscape architecture">landscape architecture</a> (pavilions, sculptures, bridges, water cascades, ponds) and vegetation (domestic and foreign species of trees and bushes). What makes this park different from other green spaces in Warsaw is the presence of peacocks and pheasants, which can be seen here walking around freely, and royal carp in the pond. Wilanów Palace Park dates back to the second half of the 17th century. It covers an area of 43 ha. Its central <a href="/wiki/Garden_%C3%A0_la_fran%C3%A7aise" class="mw-redirect" title="Garden à la française">French-styled area</a> corresponds to the ancient, Baroque forms of the palace. The eastern section of the park, closest to the Palace, is the two-level garden with a terrace facing the pond. The park around the Królikarnia Palace is situated on the old escarpment of the Vistula. The park has lanes running on a few levels deep into the ravines on both sides of the palace.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Reservoir_Warsaw.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Reservoir_Warsaw.jpg/220px-Reservoir_Warsaw.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Reservoir_Warsaw.jpg/330px-Reservoir_Warsaw.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Reservoir_Warsaw.jpg/440px-Reservoir_Warsaw.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Reservoir_Warsaw.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Saxon_Garden" title="Saxon Garden">Saxon Garden</a> with Temple of Vesta</div></div></div>
<p>Other green spaces in the city include the <a href="/wiki/Botanical_garden" title="Botanical garden">Botanic Garden</a> and the University Library garden. They have extensive botanical collection of rare domestic and foreign plants, while a <a href="/wiki/Palm_house" title="Palm house">palm house</a> in the New Orangery displays plants of subtropics from all over the world.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> Besides, within the city borders, there are also: <i>Pole Mokotowskie</i> (a big park in the northern Mokotów, where was the first horse racetrack and then the airport), <i>Park Ujazdowski</i> (close to the Sejm and John Lennon street), Park of Culture and Rest in Powsin, by the southern city border, and <i>Park Skaryszewski</i> by the right Vistula bank, in Praga. The oldest park in Praga, the <a href="/wiki/Praga_Park" title="Praga Park">Praga Park</a>, was established in 1865–1871 and designed by Jan Dobrowolski.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> In 1927 a <a href="/wiki/Zoological_garden" class="mw-redirect" title="Zoological garden">zoological garden</a> (<i>Ogród Zoologiczny</i>) was established on the park grounds,<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> and in 1952 a bear run, still open today.
</p><p>The flora of the city may be considered very rich in species. The species richness is mainly due to the location of Warsaw within the border region of several big floral regions comprising substantial proportions of close-to-wilderness areas (natural forests, wetlands along the Vistula) as well as <a href="/wiki/Arable_land" title="Arable land">arable land</a>, <a href="/wiki/Meadow" title="Meadow">meadows</a> and forests. Bielany Forest, located within the borders of Warsaw, is the remaining part of the Masovian <a href="/wiki/Old-growth_forest" title="Old-growth forest">Primeval Forest</a>. Bielany Forest nature reserve is connected with <a href="/wiki/Kampinos_Forest" title="Kampinos Forest">Kampinos Forest</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> It is home to rich fauna and flora. Within the forest there are three cycling and walking trails. Another big forest area is Kabaty Forest by the southern city border. Warsaw has also two botanic gardens: by Łazienki park (a didactic-research unit of the University of Warsaw) as well as by the Park of Culture and Rest in Powsin (a unit of the Polish Academy of Science).
</p><p>There are 13 natural reserves in Warsaw&#160;– among others, Bielany Forest, <a href="/wiki/Kabaty_Woods" title="Kabaty Woods">Kabaty Woods</a>, and Czerniaków Lake. About 15 kilometres (9 miles) from Warsaw, the <a href="/wiki/Vistula" title="Vistula">Vistula</a> river's environment changes strikingly and features a perfectly preserved <a href="/wiki/Ecosystem" title="Ecosystem">ecosystem</a>, with a habitat of animals that includes the otter, beaver and hundreds of bird species.<sup id="cite_ref-Kayaking_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kayaking-102">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> There are also several lakes in Warsaw&#160;– mainly the <a href="/wiki/Oxbow_lake" title="Oxbow lake">oxbow lakes</a>, like Czerniaków Lake, the lakes in Łazienki or Wilanów Parks, and Kamionek Lake. There are many small lakes in the parks, but only a few are permanent&#160;– the majority are emptied before winter to clean them of plants and sediments.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Zoo" title="Warsaw Zoo">Warsaw Zoo</a> covers an area of 40 hectares (99 acres).<sup id="cite_ref-zoo_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zoo-103">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> There are about 5,000 animals representing nearly 500 species.<sup id="cite_ref-zoo_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zoo-103">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> Although officially created in 1928,<sup id="cite_ref-zoo_103-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zoo-103">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> it traces back its roots to 17th century private menageries, often open to the public.<sup id="cite_ref-New_Zoo_Revue_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-New_Zoo_Revue-104">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<tr>
<td><span class="datasortkey" data-sort-value="Israel"><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flag_of_Israel.svg/21px-Flag_of_Israel.svg.png" decoding="async" width="21" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flag_of_Israel.svg/32px-Flag_of_Israel.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Flag_of_Israel.svg/41px-Flag_of_Israel.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="660" data-file-height="480" />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a></span></td>
<td>520<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><a href="/wiki/Demographics" class="mw-redirect" title="Demographics">Demographically</a>, it was the most diverse city in Poland, with significant numbers of foreign-born inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> In addition to the Polish majority, there was a significant Jewish minority in Warsaw. According to the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire_Census" title="Russian Empire Census">Russian census of 1897</a>, out of the total population of 638,000, Jews constituted 219,000 (around 34% percent).<sup id="cite_ref-Zimmerman_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zimmerman-140">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> Warsaw's prewar Jewish population of more than 350,000 constituted about 30 percent of the city's total population.<sup id="cite_ref-ushmm_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ushmm-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> In 1933, out of 1,178,914 inhabitants 833,500 were of Polish mother tongue.<sup id="cite_ref-Brockhaus_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Brockhaus-141">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> World War II changed the demographics of the city, and to this day there is much less ethnic diversity than in the previous 300 years of Warsaw's history.<sup id="cite_ref-ushmm_45-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ushmm-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Most of the modern day population growth is based on internal migration and urbanisation.
</p><p>In 1939, c. 1,300,000 people lived in Warsaw,<sup id="cite_ref-Tihran_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tihran-142">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> but in 1945&#160;– only 420,000. During the first years after the war, the population growth was c. 6%, so shortly the city started to suffer from the lack of flats and of areas for new houses. The first remedial measure was the Warsaw area enlargement (1951)&#160;– but the city authorities were still forced to introduce residency registration limitations: only the spouses and children of the permanent residents as well as some persons of public importance (like renowned specialists) were allowed to get the registration, hence halving the population growth in the following years. It also bolstered a stereotype popular among the dwellers of other cities claiming that average Varsovians thought of themselves as better only because they lived in the capital. While all restrictions on residency registration were scrapped in 1990, a negative image of a typical Warsaw inhabitant in some form persists till this day.<sup id="cite_ref-Kopinski_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kopinski-143">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Blewaska_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Blewaska-144">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Immigrant_population">Immigrant population</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Immigrant population">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Much like most capital cities in Europe, Warsaw boasts a foreign-born population that is significantly larger than in other cities, although not coming close to the figures representing the likes of <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a> or Rome. In 2016, it was estimated that 21,000 people living in Warsaw were foreign born, although some suspect the actual number could be as high as 60,000–150,000,<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> or 1.2~3.4% – 8.5% of all Varsovians. Of those, <a href="/wiki/Ukrainians_in_Poland" title="Ukrainians in Poland">Ukrainians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_people" title="Vietnamese people">Vietnamese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Byelorussians" class="mw-redirect" title="Byelorussians">Byelorussians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Russians" title="Russians">Russians</a> were the most prominent groups.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Warsaw" class="mw-redirect" title="Religion in Warsaw">Religion in Warsaw</a></div>
<p>Throughout its existence, Warsaw had been a multi-cultural city.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> According to the 1901 census, out of 711,988 inhabitants 56.2% were Catholics, 35.7% Jews, 5% Greek Orthodox Christians and 2.8% Protestants.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> Eight years later, in 1909, there were 281,754 Jews (36.9%), 18,189 Protestants (2.4%) and 2,818 <a href="/wiki/Mariavite_Church" title="Mariavite Church">Mariavites</a> (0.4%).<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> This led to construction of hundreds of places of religious worship in all parts of the town. Most of them were destroyed in the aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_uprising" class="mw-redirect" title="Warsaw uprising">Warsaw uprising</a> of 1944. After the war, the new communist authorities of Poland discouraged church construction and only a small number were rebuilt.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the survey, conducted in 2010 by a team of sociologists from <a href="/wiki/Cardinal_Stefan_Wyszy%C5%84ski_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Cardinal Stefan Wyszyński University">Cardinal Stefan Wyszyński University</a>, 66% of the Warsaw residents declared themselves as believers and 6% as non-believers. 32% of the faithful of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Warsaw" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Warsaw">Archdiocese of Warsaw</a> attended masses and 34% of the faithful of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Warszawa-Praga" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Warszawa-Praga">Warsaw-Praga diocese</a>. The Eucharist was received by about 15% of the faithful.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>As the capital of Poland, Warsaw is the political centre of the country. All state agencies are located there, including the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Poland" title="Parliament of Poland">Polish Parliament</a>, the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Poland" title="President of Poland">Presidential Office</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Poland" title="Supreme Court of Poland">Supreme Court</a>. In the Polish parliament the city and the area are represented by 31 <a href="/wiki/Member_of_Parliament" class="mw-redirect" title="Member of Parliament">MPs</a> (out of 460). Additionally, Warsaw elects two <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Member of the European Parliament">MEPs</a> (Members of the European Parliament).
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Sejm" title="Sejm">The Sejm</a> is the lower house of the Polish parliament. The Sejm is made up of 460 deputies, or Poseł in Polish (literally 'Envoy'). It is elected by universal ballot and is presided over by a speaker called the <a href="/wiki/Marshal_of_the_Sejm" title="Marshal of the Sejm">Marshal of the Sejm</a> (Marszałek Sejmu).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Municipal_government">Municipal government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Municipal government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The municipal government existed in Warsaw until World War II and was restored in 1990 (during the communist times, the National City Council&#160;– <i>Miejska Rada Narodowa</i>&#160;– governed in Warsaw). Since 1990, the system of city administration has been changed several times&#160;– also as the result of the reform which restored <i><a href="/wiki/Powiat" title="Powiat">powiat</a></i>s, cancelled in 1975. Finally, according to the <i>Warsaw Act</i>, the city is divided into 18 districts and forms one <i>city powiat</i> with a unified municipal government.<sup id="cite_ref-admin_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-admin-151">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pa%C5%82ac_Komisji_Rz%C4%85dowej_Przychod%C3%B3w_i_Skarbu_w_Warszawie_2018.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Pa%C5%82ac_Komisji_Rz%C4%85dowej_Przychod%C3%B3w_i_Skarbu_w_Warszawie_2018.jpg/220px-Pa%C5%82ac_Komisji_Rz%C4%85dowej_Przychod%C3%B3w_i_Skarbu_w_Warszawie_2018.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="119" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Pa%C5%82ac_Komisji_Rz%C4%85dowej_Przychod%C3%B3w_i_Skarbu_w_Warszawie_2018.jpg/330px-Pa%C5%82ac_Komisji_Rz%C4%85dowej_Przychod%C3%B3w_i_Skarbu_w_Warszawie_2018.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Pa%C5%82ac_Komisji_Rz%C4%85dowej_Przychod%C3%B3w_i_Skarbu_w_Warszawie_2018.jpg/440px-Pa%C5%82ac_Komisji_Rz%C4%85dowej_Przychod%C3%B3w_i_Skarbu_w_Warszawie_2018.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6322" data-file-height="3429" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pa%C5%82ac_Komisji_Rz%C4%85dowej_Przychod%C3%B3w_i_Skarbu_w_Warszawie_2018.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Neoclassical_architecture_in_Poland" title="Neoclassical architecture in Poland">Neoclassical</a> Commission Palace, the house of the city's government</div></div></div>
<p>The basic unit of territorial division in Poland is a commune (<i><a href="/wiki/Gmina" title="Gmina">gmina</a></i>).<sup id="cite_ref-altrock_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-altrock-152">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> A city is also a commune&#160;– but with a city charter.<sup id="cite_ref-altrock_152-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-altrock-152">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> Both cities and communes are governed by a mayor&#160;– but in the communes the mayor is <a href="/wiki/Vogt" title="Vogt">vogt</a> (<i>wójt</i> in Polish), however in the cities&#160;– <i>burmistrz</i>. Some bigger cities obtain the entitlements, i.e. tasks and privileges, which are possessed by the units of the second level of the territorial division&#160;– counties or <i>powiat</i>s. An example of such entitlement is a car registration: a <i>gmina</i> cannot register cars, this is a <i>powiat's</i> task (i.e. a registration number depends on what <i>powiat</i> a car had been registered in, not the <i>gmina</i>). In this case we say "city county" or <i>powiat grodzki</i>. Such cities are for example <a href="/wiki/Lublin" title="Lublin">Lublin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w" title="Kraków">Kraków</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gda%C5%84sk" title="Gdańsk">Gdańsk</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pozna%C5%84" title="Poznań">Poznań</a>. In Warsaw, its districts additionally have some of a <i>powiat</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> entitlements&#160;– like the already mentioned car registration. For example, the Wola district has its own evidence and the Ursynów district&#160;– its own (and the cars from Wola have another type of registration number than those from Ursynów). But for instance the districts in Kraków do not have the entitlements of a <i>powiat</i>, so the registration numbers in Kraków are of the same type for all districts.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dutch_Embassy_in_Warsaw_2016.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Dutch_Embassy_in_Warsaw_2016.jpg/220px-Dutch_Embassy_in_Warsaw_2016.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Dutch_Embassy_in_Warsaw_2016.jpg/330px-Dutch_Embassy_in_Warsaw_2016.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Dutch_Embassy_in_Warsaw_2016.jpg/440px-Dutch_Embassy_in_Warsaw_2016.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6133" data-file-height="4142" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dutch_Embassy_in_Warsaw_2016.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Embassy of the Netherlands</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Legislature" title="Legislature">Legislative power</a> in Warsaw is vested in a <a href="/wiki/Unicameralism" title="Unicameralism">unicameral</a> <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_City_Council" title="Warsaw City Council">Warsaw City Council</a> (<i>Rada Miasta</i>), which comprises 60 members.<sup id="cite_ref-admin_151-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-admin-151">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> Council members are elected directly every four years. Like most legislative bodies, the city council divides itself into committees which have the oversight of various functions of the city government.<sup id="cite_ref-admin_151-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-admin-151">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> Bills passed by a simple majority are sent to the mayor (the <a href="/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_Warsaw" title="List of mayors of Warsaw">President of Warsaw</a>), who may sign them into law. If the mayor vetoes a bill, the Council has 30 days to override the veto by a two-thirds majority vote.
</p><p>Each of the 18 separate city districts has its own council (<i>Rada dzielnicy</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-admin_151-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-admin-151">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> Their duties are focused on aiding the President and the City Council, as well as supervising various municipal companies, city-owned property and schools. The head of each of the District Councils is named the Mayor (<i>Burmistrz</i>) and is elected by the local council from the candidates proposed by the President of Warsaw.
</p><p>The mayor of Warsaw is called President. Generally, in Poland, the mayors of bigger cities are called <i>presidents</i>&#160;– i.e. cities with over 100,000 people or that had a president before 1990. The first Warsaw President was Jan Andrzej Menich (1695–1696).<sup id="cite_ref-Petrozolin_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Petrozolin-153">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> Between 1975 and 1990 the Warsaw presidents simultaneously led the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Voivodeship_(1975-1998)" class="mw-redirect" title="Warsaw Voivodeship (1975-1998)">Warsaw Voivode</a>. Since 1990 the President of Warsaw had been elected by the <a href="/wiki/City_council" title="City council">city council</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-djordjevic_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-djordjevic-154">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> In the years of 1994–1999 the mayor of the district Centrum automatically was designated as the President of Warsaw: the mayor of Centrum was elected by the district council of Centrum and the council was elected only by the Centrum residents. Since 2002 the President of Warsaw is elected by all of the citizens of Warsaw.<sup id="cite_ref-djordjevic_154-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-djordjevic-154">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The current <a href="/wiki/List_of_mayors_of_Warsaw" title="List of mayors of Warsaw">President of Warsaw</a> is <a href="/wiki/Rafa%C5%82_Trzaskowski" title="Rafał Trzaskowski">Rafał Trzaskowski</a>. The first president elected according these rules was <a href="/wiki/Lech_Kaczy%C5%84ski" title="Lech Kaczyński">Lech Kaczyński</a>. When he was elected as the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Poland" title="President of Poland">President of Polish Republic</a> (December 2005) he resigned as mayor on the day before taking office.
</p>

		</div></li>
</ul>

</p>
<div style="position:absolute; left:149px; top:62px"><a href="/wiki/Bia%C5%82o%C5%82%C4%99ka" title="Białołęka">Białołęka</a></div>

<div style="position:absolute; left:206px; top:142px"><a href="/wiki/Targ%C3%B3wek" title="Targówek">Targówek</a></div>
<div style="position:absolute; left:161px; top:215px"><a href="/wiki/%C5%9Ar%C3%B3dmie%C5%9Bcie,_Warsaw" title="Śródmieście, Warsaw">Śródmieście</a></div>
<div style="position:absolute; left:121px; top:215px"><a href="/wiki/Wola" title="Wola">Wola</a></div>

<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<p>Until 1994, there were 7 districts in Warsaw: Śródmieście, Praga Północ, Praga Południe, Żoliborz, Wola, Ochota, and Mokotów. Between 1994 and 2002, there were 11 districts: Centrum, Białołęka, Targówek, Rembertów, Wawer, Wilanów, Ursynów, Włochy, Ursus, Bemowo, and Bielany. In 2002, the town <a href="/wiki/Weso%C5%82a" title="Wesoła">Wesoła</a> was incorporated and the territorial division of Warsaw was established as follows:
</p><p>Warsaw is a county (<i><a href="/wiki/Powiat" title="Powiat">powiat</a></i>), and is further divided into 18 districts (<i>dzielnica</i>),<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> each one with its own administrative body.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> Each of the districts is customarily subdivided into several neighbourhoods which have no legal or administrative status. Warsaw has two historic neighbourhoods, called <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Old_Town" title="Warsaw Old Town">Old Town</a> (<i>Stare Miasto</i>) and <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_New_Town" title="Warsaw New Town">New Town</a> (<i>Nowe Miasto</i>), in the borough of <a href="/wiki/%C5%9Ar%C3%B3dmie%C5%9Bcie,_Warsaw" title="Śródmieście, Warsaw">Śródmieście</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Poland" title="Economy of Poland">Economy of Poland</a></div>
<p>In 2011, Warsaw was ranked the world's 46th most expensive city to live in.<sup id="cite_ref-glob_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-glob-159">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> It was classified as an <a href="/wiki/Global_city" title="Global city">alpha</a> world city (also known as a "major global city that links economic regions into the world economy") by the Globalization and World Cities (GaWC) Study Group and Network from <a href="/wiki/Loughborough_University" title="Loughborough University">Loughborough University</a>, placing it on a par with cities such as <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">Sydney</a>, <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">Istanbul</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a> or <a href="/wiki/Seoul" title="Seoul">Seoul</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Business_and_commerce">Business and commerce</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Business and commerce">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Centro_Comercial_Terrazas_de_Oro_en_Varsovia.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Centro_Comercial_Terrazas_de_Oro_en_Varsovia.JPG/220px-Centro_Comercial_Terrazas_de_Oro_en_Varsovia.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Centro_Comercial_Terrazas_de_Oro_en_Varsovia.JPG/330px-Centro_Comercial_Terrazas_de_Oro_en_Varsovia.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Centro_Comercial_Terrazas_de_Oro_en_Varsovia.JPG/440px-Centro_Comercial_Terrazas_de_Oro_en_Varsovia.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Centro_Comercial_Terrazas_de_Oro_en_Varsovia.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Z%C5%82ote_Tarasy" title="Złote Tarasy">Złote Tarasy</a></i> (Golden Terraces) is a commercial and entertainment complex in the center of Warsaw.</div></div></div>
<p>Warsaw, especially its city centre (<a href="/wiki/%C5%9Ar%C3%B3dmie%C5%9Bcie,_Warsaw" title="Śródmieście, Warsaw"><i>Śródmieście</i></a>), is home not only to many national institutions and government agencies, but also to many domestic and international companies. In 2006, 304,016 companies were registered in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-stat_gov_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stat_gov-160">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> Warsaw's ever-growing business community has been noticed globally, regionally, and nationally. MasterCard Emerging Market Index has noted Warsaw's economic strength and commercial center. Warsaw was ranked as the seventh-greatest emerging market. Foreign investors' financial participation in the city's development was estimated in 2002 at over 650&#160;million <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">€</a>.
</p><p>Warsaw produces 12% of Poland's national income,<sup id="cite_ref-cityreport_161-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cityreport-161">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> which in 2008 was 305.1% of the Polish average per capita (or 160% of the European Union average). The <a href="/wiki/Nominal_GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="Nominal GDP">Nominal GDP</a> per capita in Warsaw amounted to 140,000 <a href="/wiki/Polish_Zloty" class="mw-redirect" title="Polish Zloty">Polish Zloty</a> in 2017 (c. €32,500 or around <a href="/wiki/USD" class="mw-redirect" title="USD">$</a>80,000 in <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_Power_Parity" class="mw-redirect" title="Purchasing Power Parity">PPP</a><sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>)<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>. Warsaw leads <a href="/wiki/East-Central_Europe" title="East-Central Europe">East-Central Europe</a> in foreign investment and in 2006, GDP growth met expectations with a level of 6.1%.<sup id="cite_ref-pmrconsulting_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pmrconsulting-164">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> It also has one of the fastest growing economies, with GDP growth at 6.5 percent in 2007 and 6.1 percent in the first quarter of 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-CEE_165-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CEE-165">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the same time the unemployment rate is one of the lowest in Poland, at around 4% in February 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> The city itself receives around 8,740,882,000 <a href="/wiki/Polish_z%C5%82oty" title="Polish złoty">złotys</a> in taxes and direct government grants.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Warsaw_Stock_Exchange">Warsaw Stock Exchange</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Warsaw Stock Exchange">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Stock_Exchange" title="Warsaw Stock Exchange">Warsaw Stock Exchange</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Centrum_Gie%C5%82dowe_w_Warszawie_07.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Centrum_Gie%C5%82dowe_w_Warszawie_07.jpg/220px-Centrum_Gie%C5%82dowe_w_Warszawie_07.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Centrum_Gie%C5%82dowe_w_Warszawie_07.jpg/330px-Centrum_Gie%C5%82dowe_w_Warszawie_07.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Centrum_Gie%C5%82dowe_w_Warszawie_07.jpg/440px-Centrum_Gie%C5%82dowe_w_Warszawie_07.jpg 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="540" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Centrum_Gie%C5%82dowe_w_Warszawie_07.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Stock_Exchange" title="Warsaw Stock Exchange">Warsaw Stock Exchange</a> is the largest in Central Europe.</div></div></div>
<p>Warsaw's first <a href="/wiki/Stock_exchange" title="Stock exchange">stock exchange</a> was established in 1817 and continued trading until World War II. It was re-established in April 1991, following the end of the post-war communist control of the country and the reintroduction of a <a href="/wiki/Free_market" title="Free market">free-market economy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-stock_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stock-167">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> Today, the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Stock_Exchange" title="Warsaw Stock Exchange">Warsaw Stock Exchange</a> (WSE) is, according to many indicators,<sup id="cite_ref-CEE_165-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CEE-165">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> the largest market in the region, with 374 companies listed and total capitalization of 162,584 mln EUR as of 31 August 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-gpw_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gpw-168">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> From 1991 until 2000, the stock exchange was, ironically, located in the building previously used as the headquarters of the Polish United Workers' Party (<a href="/wiki/Polish_United_Workers%27_Party" title="Polish United Workers&#39; Party">PZPR</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-Tourism_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tourism-169">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Industry">Industry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Industry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During Warsaw's reconstruction after World War II, the communist authorities decided that the city would become a major industrial centre. As a result, numerous large factories were built in and around the city. The largest were the <i>Huta Warszawa</i> Steel Works, the <a href="/wiki/Fabryka_Samochod%C3%B3w_Osobowych" title="Fabryka Samochodów Osobowych">FSO</a> car factory and the "Ursus" tractor factory.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Budynek_rektyfikacji_Koneser_2018.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Budynek_rektyfikacji_Koneser_2018.jpg/220px-Budynek_rektyfikacji_Koneser_2018.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Budynek_rektyfikacji_Koneser_2018.jpg/330px-Budynek_rektyfikacji_Koneser_2018.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Budynek_rektyfikacji_Koneser_2018.jpg/440px-Budynek_rektyfikacji_Koneser_2018.jpg 2x" data-file-width="726" data-file-height="501" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Budynek_rektyfikacji_Koneser_2018.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Praga_Koneser_Center" title="Praga Koneser Center">Praga Koneser Center</a> within the former <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Vodka_Factory_%22Koneser%22" title="Warsaw Vodka Factory &quot;Koneser&quot;">Warsaw Vodka Factory</a></div></div></div>
<p>As the communist economy deteriorated, these factories lost significance and most went bankrupt after 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-industry_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-industry-170">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Parysek_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Parysek-171">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> Today, the <a href="/wiki/ArcelorMittal" title="ArcelorMittal">Arcelor</a> Warszawa <a href="/wiki/Steel_mill" title="Steel mill">Steel mill</a> (formerly <i>Huta Warszawa</i>) is the only major factory remaining.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Fabryka_Samochod%C3%B3w_Osobowych" title="Fabryka Samochodów Osobowych">FSO Car Factory</a> was established in 1951. A number of vehicles have been assembled there over the decades, including the <a href="/wiki/FSO_Warszawa" title="FSO Warszawa">Warszawa</a>, <a href="/wiki/FSO_Syrena" title="FSO Syrena">Syrena</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polski_Fiat_125p" title="Polski Fiat 125p">Fiat 125p</a> (under license from Fiat, later renamed FSO 125p when the license expired) and the <a href="/wiki/FSO_Polonez" title="FSO Polonez">Polonez</a>. The last two models listed were also sent abroad and assembled in a number of other countries, including Egypt and Colombia. In 1995 the factory was purchased by the South Korean car manufacturer <a href="/wiki/Daewoo" title="Daewoo">Daewoo</a>, which assembled the Tico, Espero, Nubia, Tacuma, Leganza, Lanos and Matiz there for the European market. In 2005 the factory was sold to <a href="/wiki/AvtoZAZ" title="AvtoZAZ">AvtoZAZ</a>, a Ukrainian car manufacturer which assembled the Chevrolet Aveo there. The license for the production of the Aveo expired in February 2011 and has not been renewed since. Currently the company is defunct.
</p><p>The "<a href="/wiki/Ursus_Factory" class="mw-redirect" title="Ursus Factory">Ursus</a>" factory opened in 1893 and is still in operation. Throughout its history various machinery was assembled there, including motorcycles, military vehicles, trucks and buses; but since World War II it has produced only tractors.
</p><p>The number of state-owned enterprises continues to decrease while the number of companies operating with foreign capital is on the rise, reflecting the continued shift towards a modern market-based economy.<sup id="cite_ref-industry_170-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-industry-170">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> The largest foreign investors are <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola_Amatil" title="Coca-Cola Amatil">Coca-Cola Amatil</a> and <a href="/wiki/Metro_AG" title="Metro AG">Metro AG</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-industry_170-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-industry-170">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> Warsaw has the biggest concentration of electronics and high-tech industry in Poland, while the growing consumer market perfectly fosters the development of the food-processing industry.<sup id="cite_ref-industry_170-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-industry-170">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Warsaw" title="Education in Warsaw">Education in Warsaw</a></div>
<table style="float:right;">
<tbody><tr>
<td><div class="mw-collapsible mw-collapsed" style="box-sizing:border-box;width:100%;font-size:95%;padding:4px;border:none;"><div style="font-size:100%;line-height:1.6;font-weight:bold;background:transparent;text-align:center;;width: 325px; background: #B5B5B5;">Higher education in Warsaw</div><div class="mw-collapsible-content" style="background:transparent;text-align:left;;">
<p>&#160;&#160;&#160;<b>Name and year established</b>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Warsaw" title="University of Warsaw">University of Warsaw</a> (1816)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Warsaw_University_of_Technology" title="Warsaw University of Technology">Warsaw University of Technology</a> (1826)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Warsaw_School_of_Economics" class="mw-redirect" title="Warsaw School of Economics">Warsaw School of Economics</a> (1906)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Warsaw_University_of_Life_Sciences" title="Warsaw University of Life Sciences">Warsaw University of Life Sciences</a> (1818)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cardinal_Stefan_Wyszy%C5%84ski_University_in_Warsaw" title="Cardinal Stefan Wyszyński University in Warsaw">Cardinal Stefan Wyszyński University</a> (1999)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Medical_University_of_Warsaw" title="Medical University of Warsaw">Medical University of Warsaw</a> (1809/1950)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Fine_Arts_in_Warsaw" title="Academy of Fine Arts in Warsaw">Academy of Fine Arts</a> (1844)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/National_Defence_University_in_Warsaw" class="mw-redirect" title="National Defence University in Warsaw">Academy of National Defence</a> (1947/1990)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Military_University_of_Technology_in_Warsaw" class="mw-redirect" title="Military University of Technology in Warsaw">Military University of Technology</a> (1951)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/J%C3%B3zef_Pi%C5%82sudski_University_of_Physical_Education_in_Warsaw" title="Józef Piłsudski University of Physical Education in Warsaw">University of Physical Education in Warsaw</a> (1929)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fryderyk_Chopin_University_of_Music" title="Fryderyk Chopin University of Music">Fryderyk Chopin University of Music</a> (1810)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kozminski_University" title="Kozminski University">Kozminski University</a> (1993)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Social_Sciences_and_Humanities" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Social Sciences and Humanities">University of Social Sciences and Humanities</a> (1996)</li></ul></div></div>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Warsaw holds some of the finest institutions of higher education in Poland. It is home to four major universities and over 62 smaller schools of higher education.<sup id="cite_ref-gus_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gus-172">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> The overall number of students of all grades of education in Warsaw is almost 500,000 (29.2% of the city population; 2002). The number of university students is over 280,000.<sup id="cite_ref-Studia_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Studia-173">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> Most of the reputable universities are public, but in recent years there has also been an upsurge in the number of private universities.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Brama_Uniwersytetu_Warszawskiego.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Brama_Uniwersytetu_Warszawskiego.jpg/220px-Brama_Uniwersytetu_Warszawskiego.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Brama_Uniwersytetu_Warszawskiego.jpg/330px-Brama_Uniwersytetu_Warszawskiego.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Brama_Uniwersytetu_Warszawskiego.jpg/440px-Brama_Uniwersytetu_Warszawskiego.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4358" data-file-height="2903" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Brama_Uniwersytetu_Warszawskiego.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The main gate of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Warsaw" title="University of Warsaw">University of Warsaw</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pasteura_5.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Pasteura_5.jpg/220px-Pasteura_5.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Pasteura_5.jpg/330px-Pasteura_5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Pasteura_5.jpg/440px-Pasteura_5.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4555" data-file-height="3314" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pasteura_5.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Faculty of Physics of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Warsaw" title="University of Warsaw">University of Warsaw</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Warsaw" title="University of Warsaw">University of Warsaw</a> was established in 1816, when the partitions of Poland separated Warsaw from the oldest and most influential Polish academic center, in <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w" title="Kraków">Kraków</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-uw_edu_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uw_edu-174">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_University_of_Technology" title="Warsaw University of Technology">Warsaw University of Technology</a> is the second academic school of technology in the country, and one of the largest in <a href="/wiki/East-Central_Europe" title="East-Central Europe">East-Central Europe</a>, employing 2,000 professors.<sup id="cite_ref-onelab_175-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-onelab-175">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> Other institutions for higher education include the <a href="/wiki/Medical_University_of_Warsaw" title="Medical University of Warsaw">Medical University of Warsaw</a>, the largest medical school in Poland and one of the most prestigious; the <a href="/wiki/Defense_(military)" class="mw-redirect" title="Defense (military)">National Defence</a> University, highest military academic institution in Poland; the <a href="/wiki/Fryderyk_Chopin_University_of_Music" title="Fryderyk Chopin University of Music">Fryderyk Chopin University of Music</a>, the oldest and largest music school in Poland and one of the largest in Europe;<sup id="cite_ref-infochopin_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-infochopin-176">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_School_of_Economics" class="mw-redirect" title="Warsaw School of Economics">Warsaw School of Economics</a>, the oldest and most renowned economic university in the country;<sup id="cite_ref-sgh_waw_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sgh_waw-177">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_University_of_Life_Sciences" title="Warsaw University of Life Sciences">Warsaw University of Life Sciences</a>, the largest agricultural university, founded in 1818;<sup id="cite_ref-sggw_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sggw-178">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Social_Sciences_and_Humanities" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Social Sciences and Humanities">University of Social Sciences and Humanities</a>, the first private secular university in the country.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:6_Warszawa_411.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/6_Warszawa_411.jpg/220px-6_Warszawa_411.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/6_Warszawa_411.jpg/330px-6_Warszawa_411.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/6_Warszawa_411.jpg/440px-6_Warszawa_411.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="483" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:6_Warszawa_411.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Warsaw_University_Library" title="Warsaw University Library">Warsaw University Library</a></div></div></div>
<p>Warsaw has numerous libraries, many of which contain vast collections of historic documents. The most important library in terms of historic document collections is the <a href="/wiki/National_Library_of_Poland" title="National Library of Poland">National Library of Poland</a>. The library holds 8.2&#160;million volumes in its collection.<sup id="cite_ref-bn_org_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bn_org-179">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> Formed in 1928,<sup id="cite_ref-fyifrance_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fyifrance-180">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> it sees itself as a successor to the <a href="/wiki/Za%C5%82uski_Library" title="Załuski Library">Załuski Library</a>, the biggest in Poland and one of the first and biggest libraries in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-fyifrance_180-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fyifrance-180">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-utoronto_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-utoronto-181">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Another important library – the University Library, founded in 1816,<sup id="cite_ref-buw_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-buw-182">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> is home to over two million items.<sup id="cite_ref-Zbiory_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zbiory-183">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> The building was designed by architects Marek Budzyński and Zbigniew Badowski and opened on 15 December 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-Library_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Library-184">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> It is surrounded by green. The University Library garden, designed by Irena Bajerska, was opened on 12 June 2002. It is one of the largest and most beautiful roof gardens in Europe with an area of more than 10,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup> (110,000&#160;sq&#160;ft), and plants covering 5,111&#160;m<sup>2</sup> (55,010&#160;sq&#160;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-garden_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-garden-185">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> As the university garden it is open to the public every day.<sup id="cite_ref-garden_185-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-garden-185">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport_and_infrastructure">Transport and infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Transport and infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Warsaw" title="Transport in Warsaw">Transport in Warsaw</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Stadion_Narodowy_-_Wisla.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Stadion_Narodowy_-_Wisla.jpg/220px-Stadion_Narodowy_-_Wisla.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="118" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Stadion_Narodowy_-_Wisla.jpg/330px-Stadion_Narodowy_-_Wisla.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/Stadion_Narodowy_-_Wisla.jpg/440px-Stadion_Narodowy_-_Wisla.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4162" data-file-height="2239" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Stadion_Narodowy_-_Wisla.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Night view of the <a href="/wiki/%C5%9Awi%C4%99tokrzyski_Bridge" title="Świętokrzyski Bridge">Świętokrzyski Bridge</a> and the <a href="/wiki/National_Stadium,_Warsaw" title="National Stadium, Warsaw">National Stadium</a> from the left bank of the Vistula</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:POL_Warszawa_S8_05.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/POL_Warszawa_S8_05.jpg/220px-POL_Warszawa_S8_05.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/POL_Warszawa_S8_05.jpg/330px-POL_Warszawa_S8_05.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/POL_Warszawa_S8_05.jpg/440px-POL_Warszawa_S8_05.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:POL_Warszawa_S8_05.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Expressway_S8_(Poland)" title="Expressway S8 (Poland)">S8</a> in Warsaw</div></div></div>
<p>Warsaw has seen major infrastructural changes over the past few years amidst increased foreign investment, economic growth and EU funding. The city has a much improved infrastructure with new roads, <a href="/wiki/Overpass" title="Overpass">flyovers</a>, bridges, etc.<sup id="cite_ref-Jeziorski_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jeziorski-186">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Warsaw lacks a complete <a href="/wiki/Ring_road" title="Ring road">ring road</a> system and most traffic goes directly through the city centre, leading to the eleventh highest level of congestion in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> The Warsaw ring road has been planned to consist of three <a href="/wiki/Expressways_of_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="Expressways of Poland">express roads</a>: <a href="/wiki/Expressway_S2_(Poland)" title="Expressway S2 (Poland)">S2</a> (south), <a href="/wiki/Expressway_S8_(Poland)" title="Expressway S8 (Poland)">S8</a> (north-west) and <a href="/wiki/Expressway_S17_(Poland)" title="Expressway S17 (Poland)">S17</a> (east). Currently S8 and a part of S2 are open, with S2 to be finished by 2020<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup>.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Autostrada_A2" class="mw-redirect" title="Autostrada A2">A2 motorway</a> opened in June 2012, stretches west from Warsaw and is a direct motorway connection with Łódź, Poznań and ultimately with Berlin.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lotnisko_Chopina_w_Warszawie_2018b.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Lotnisko_Chopina_w_Warszawie_2018b.jpg/220px-Lotnisko_Chopina_w_Warszawie_2018b.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="127" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Lotnisko_Chopina_w_Warszawie_2018b.jpg/330px-Lotnisko_Chopina_w_Warszawie_2018b.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Lotnisko_Chopina_w_Warszawie_2018b.jpg/440px-Lotnisko_Chopina_w_Warszawie_2018b.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6664" data-file-height="3856" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lotnisko_Chopina_w_Warszawie_2018b.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Chopin_Airport" title="Warsaw Chopin Airport">Warsaw Chopin Airport</a></div></div></div>
<p>The city has two <a href="/wiki/International_airports" class="mw-redirect" title="International airports">international airports</a>: <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Chopin_Airport" title="Warsaw Chopin Airport">Warsaw Chopin Airport</a>, located just 10 kilometres (6.2&#160;mi) from the city centre, and <a href="/wiki/Modlin_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Modlin Airport">Warsaw-Modlin Airport</a>, located 35 kilometres (22&#160;mi) to the north, opened in July 2012. With around 100 international and domestic flights a day and with 15 500 000 passengers served in 2017, Warsaw Frédéric Chopin Airport is by far the biggest airport in Poland and in Central-Eastern Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-airport_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-airport-189">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> and it has also been called "the most important and largest airport in Central Europe".<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tram_in_Warsaw.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Tram_in_Warsaw.jpg/170px-Tram_in_Warsaw.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Tram_in_Warsaw.jpg/255px-Tram_in_Warsaw.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Tram_in_Warsaw.jpg/340px-Tram_in_Warsaw.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2885" data-file-height="3846" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tram_in_Warsaw.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Trams_in_Warsaw" title="Trams in Warsaw">Tram car</a></div></div></div>
<p>Public transport in Warsaw includes <a href="/wiki/Bus_transport_in_Warsaw" title="Bus transport in Warsaw">buses</a>, <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Tramway" class="mw-redirect" title="Warsaw Tramway">trams</a> (<a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">streetcars</a>), <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Metro" title="Warsaw Metro">Metro</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Light_rail" title="Light rail">light rail</a> <a href="/wiki/Warszawska_Kolej_Dojazdowa" class="mw-redirect" title="Warszawska Kolej Dojazdowa">Warszawska Kolej Dojazdowa</a> line, urban railway <a href="/wiki/Szybka_Kolej_Miejska_(Warsaw)" title="Szybka Kolej Miejska (Warsaw)">Szybka Kolej Miejska</a>, <a href="/wiki/Regional_rail" title="Regional rail">regional rail</a> <a href="/wiki/Koleje_Mazowieckie" title="Koleje Mazowieckie">Koleje Mazowieckie</a> (Mazovian Railways),<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Bicycle_sharing_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Bicycle sharing system">bicycle sharing systems</a> (<a href="/wiki/Veturilo" title="Veturilo">Veturilo</a>). The buses, trams, urban railway and Metro are managed by <a href="/wiki/Zarz%C4%85d_Transportu_Miejskiego" class="mw-redirect" title="Zarząd Transportu Miejskiego">Zarząd Transportu Miejskiego</a> (<i>ZTM</i>, the Warsaw Municipal Transport Authority).
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ED250-010.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/ED250-010.jpg/220px-ED250-010.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/ED250-010.jpg/330px-ED250-010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/ED250-010.jpg/440px-ED250-010.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ED250-010.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Pendolino" title="Pendolino">Pendolino</a> <a href="/wiki/High-speed_rail" title="High-speed rail">high-speed trains</a> connect Warsaw, <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w" title="Kraków">Kraków</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wroc%C5%82aw" title="Wrocław">Wrocław</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tricity,_Poland" title="Tricity, Poland">Tri-City</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Upper_Silesian_metropolitan_area" title="Upper Silesian metropolitan area">Upper Silesian metropolitan area</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The regional rail and light rail is operated by <a href="/wiki/Polish_State_Railways" title="Polish State Railways">Polish State Railways</a> (PKP). There are also some suburban bus lines run by private operators.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bus_transport_in_Warsaw" title="Bus transport in Warsaw">Bus</a> service covers the entire city, with approximately 170 routes totalling about 2,603 kilometres (1,617&#160;mi), and with some 1,600 vehicles.
</p><p>Currently, the <i>Tramwaje Warszawskie</i> (Warsaw Trams) company runs 863 cars on over 240 kilometres (150&#160;mi) of tracks. Twenty-odd lines run across the city with additional lines opened on special occasions (such as <a href="/wiki/All_Saints%27_Day" title="All Saints&#39; Day">All Saints' Day</a>).
</p><p>The first section of the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Metro" title="Warsaw Metro">Warsaw Metro</a> was opened in 1995 initially with a total of 11 stations.<sup id="cite_ref-metro_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-metro-193">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> It now has 21 stations running a distance of approximately 23&#160;km (14&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup> Initially, all of the trains were <a href="/wiki/Metrowagonmash" title="Metrowagonmash">Russian built</a>. In 1998, 108 new carriages were ordered from <a href="/wiki/Alstom" title="Alstom">Alstom</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-metro_193-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-metro-193">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> The second line running east-west will be about 31&#160;km (19&#160;mi). The central section is 6&#160;km (4&#160;mi) long with seven stations,<sup id="cite_ref-metro_193-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-metro-193">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> opened on 8 March 2015.
</p><p>The main railway station is <a href="/wiki/Warszawa_Centralna_railway_station" title="Warszawa Centralna railway station">Warszawa Centralna</a> serving both domestic traffic to almost every major city in Poland, and international connections. There are also five other major railway stations and a number of smaller suburban stations.
</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">
	<li class="gallerycaption">Public transport in Warsaw</li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 182px"><div style="width: 182px">
