<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Infrastructure_in_Warsaw" title="Infrastructure in Warsaw">Infrastructure in Warsaw</a></div>
<p>Like many cities in <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central</a> and Eastern Europe, infrastructure in Warsaw suffered considerably during its time as an <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Bloc_economies" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Bloc economies">Eastern Bloc economy</a> – though it is worth mentioning that the initial <a href="/wiki/Three-Year_Plan" title="Three-Year Plan">Three-Year Plan</a> to rebuild Poland (especially Warsaw) was a major success, but what followed was very much the opposite. However, over the past decade Warsaw has seen many improvements due to solid economic growth, an increase in <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">foreign investment</a> as well as funding from the European Union. In particular, the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Metro" title="Warsaw Metro">city's metro</a>, roads, sidewalks, health care facilities and sanitation facilities have improved markedly.<sup id="cite_ref-Jeziorski_186-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jeziorski-186">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Today, Warsaw has some of the best medical facilities in Poland and <a href="/wiki/East-Central_Europe" title="East-Central Europe">East-Central Europe</a>. The city is home to the <a href="/wiki/Children%27s_Memorial_Health_Institute" title="Children&#39;s Memorial Health Institute">Children's Memorial Health Institute</a> (CMHI), the highest-reference hospital in all of Poland, as well as an active research and education center.<sup id="cite_ref-cmhi_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cmhi-195">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Curie_Institute_(Warsaw)" class="mw-redirect" title="Curie Institute (Warsaw)">Maria Skłodowska-Curie Institute of Oncology</a> is one of the largest and most modern oncological institutions in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-apta_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-apta-196">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> The clinical section is located in a 10-floor building with 700 beds, 10 operating theatres, an intensive-care unit, several diagnostic departments as well as an outpatient clinic.<sup id="cite_ref-apta_196-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-apta-196">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup>
The infrastructure has developed a lot over the past years.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_and_theatre">Music and theatre</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Music and theatre">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Warszawa,_ul._Senatorska_21,_25_20170516_001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Warszawa%2C_ul._Senatorska_21%2C_25_20170516_001.jpg/250px-Warszawa%2C_ul._Senatorska_21%2C_25_20170516_001.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Warszawa%2C_ul._Senatorska_21%2C_25_20170516_001.jpg/375px-Warszawa%2C_ul._Senatorska_21%2C_25_20170516_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Warszawa%2C_ul._Senatorska_21%2C_25_20170516_001.jpg/500px-Warszawa%2C_ul._Senatorska_21%2C_25_20170516_001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5996" data-file-height="4003" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Warszawa,_ul._Senatorska_21,_25_20170516_001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The edifice of the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Theatre,_Warsaw" title="Grand Theatre, Warsaw">Grand Theatre</a> in Warsaw. It is one of the largest theatres in Europe, featuring one of the biggest stages in the world.</div></div></div>
<p>Thanks to numerous musical venues, including the <a href="/wiki/Great_Theatre,_Warsaw" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Theatre, Warsaw"><i>Teatr Wielki</i>, the Polish National Opera</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Chamber_opera" title="Chamber opera">Chamber Opera</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Philharmonic_Orchestra" class="mw-redirect" title="Warsaw Philharmonic Orchestra">National Philharmonic Hall</a> and the <a href="/wiki/National_Theatre,_Warsaw" title="National Theatre, Warsaw">National Theatre</a>, as well as the Roma and Buffo music theatres and the <a href="/wiki/Congress_Hall_(Warsaw)" title="Congress Hall (Warsaw)">Congress Hall</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Culture_and_Science,_Warsaw" class="mw-redirect" title="Palace of Culture and Science, Warsaw">Palace of Culture and Science</a>, Warsaw hosts many events and festivals. Among the events worth particular attention are: the <a href="/wiki/International_Fr%C3%A9d%C3%A9ric_Chopin_Piano_Competition" class="mw-redirect" title="International Frédéric Chopin Piano Competition">International Frédéric Chopin Piano Competition</a>, the International Contemporary Music Festival <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Autumn" title="Warsaw Autumn">Warsaw Autumn</a>, the Jazz Jamboree, Warsaw Summer Jazz Days, the International <a href="/wiki/Stanis%C5%82aw_Moniuszko" title="Stanisław Moniuszko">Stanisław Moniuszko</a> Vocal Competition, the Mozart Festival, and the Festival of Old Music.<sup id="cite_ref-salter_198-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-salter-198">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Warsaw is also considered as one of the European hubs of underground electronic music with a very attractive house and techno music scene.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Warsaw is home to over 30 major theatres spread throughout the city, including the <a href="/wiki/National_Theatre,_Warsaw" title="National Theatre, Warsaw">National Theatre</a> (founded in 1765) and the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Theatre,_Warsaw" title="Grand Theatre, Warsaw">Grand Theatre</a> (established 1778).<sup id="cite_ref-teatrwielki1_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-teatrwielki1-200">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chopin_Competition_2015_Finals.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Chopin_Competition_2015_Finals.jpg/220px-Chopin_Competition_2015_Finals.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Chopin_Competition_2015_Finals.jpg/330px-Chopin_Competition_2015_Finals.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/Chopin_Competition_2015_Finals.jpg/440px-Chopin_Competition_2015_Finals.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chopin_Competition_2015_Finals.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>2015 <a href="/wiki/International_Chopin_Piano_Competition" title="International Chopin Piano Competition">International Chopin Piano Competition</a> Finals in Warsaw</div></div></div>
<p>Warsaw also attracts many young and off-stream directors and performers who add to the city's theatrical culture. Their productions may be viewed mostly in smaller theatres and <i>Houses of Culture</i> (<i>Domy Kultury</i>), mostly outside <i><a href="/wiki/%C5%9Ar%C3%B3dmie%C5%9Bcie,_Warsaw" title="Śródmieście, Warsaw">Śródmieście</a></i> (Central Warsaw). Warsaw hosts the International Theatrical Meetings.
</p><p>From 1833 to the outbreak of World War II, Plac Teatralny <i>(<a href="/wiki/Theatre_Square_(Warsaw)" title="Theatre Square (Warsaw)">Theatre Square</a>)</i> was the country's cultural hub and home to the various theatres.<sup id="cite_ref-teatrwielki_201-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-teatrwielki-201">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup> Plac Teatralny and its environs was the venue for numerous parades, celebrations of state holidays, carnival balls and concerts.
</p><p>The main building housed the <a href="/wiki/Great_Theatre,_Warsaw" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Theatre, Warsaw">Great Theatre</a> from 1833 to 1834, the Rozmaitości Theatre from 1836 to 1924 and then the National Theatre, the Reduta Theatre from 1919 to 1924, and from 1928 to 1939&#160;&#8211;&#32;the Nowy Theatre, which staged productions of contemporary poetical drama, including those directed by <a href="/wiki/Leon_Schiller" title="Leon Schiller">Leon Schiller</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-teatrwielki_201-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-teatrwielki-201">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Nearby, in Ogród Saski (the <a href="/wiki/Saxon_Garden" title="Saxon Garden">Saxon Garden</a>), the Summer Theatre was in operation from 1870 to 1939,<sup id="cite_ref-Letni_202-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Letni-202">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> and in the <a href="/wiki/Interwar_period" title="Interwar period">inter-war period</a>, the theatre complex also included Momus, Warsaw's first literary cabaret, and <a href="/wiki/Leon_Schiller" title="Leon Schiller">Leon Schiller</a>'s musical theatre Melodram. The <a href="/wiki/Wojciech_Bogus%C5%82awski" title="Wojciech Bogusławski">Wojciech Bogusławski</a> Theatre (1922–26) was the best example of "Polish monumental theatre". From the mid-1930s, the Great Theatre building housed the Upati Institute of Dramatic Arts&#160;&#8211;&#32;the first state-run academy of dramatic art, with an acting department and a stage directing department.<sup id="cite_ref-teatrwielki_201-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-teatrwielki-201">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Events">Events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Warsaw_Multimedia_Fountain_Park_1.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Warsaw_Multimedia_Fountain_Park_1.JPG/220px-Warsaw_Multimedia_Fountain_Park_1.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Warsaw_Multimedia_Fountain_Park_1.JPG/330px-Warsaw_Multimedia_Fountain_Park_1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Warsaw_Multimedia_Fountain_Park_1.JPG/440px-Warsaw_Multimedia_Fountain_Park_1.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4447" data-file-height="2991" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Warsaw_Multimedia_Fountain_Park_1.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Warsaw Multimedia Fountain Park</div></div></div>
<p>Several commemorative events take place every year. Gatherings of thousands of people on the banks of the Vistula on Midsummer's Night for a festival called <a href="/wiki/Wianki" title="Wianki">Wianki</a> (Polish for <i>Wreaths</i>) have become a tradition and a yearly event in the programme of cultural events in Warsaw.<sup id="cite_ref-sobotka_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sobotka-203">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wreath_204-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wreath-204">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> The festival traces its roots to a peaceful <a href="/wiki/Paganism" title="Paganism">pagan</a> ritual where maidens would float their <a href="/wiki/Wreath" title="Wreath">wreaths</a> of herbs on the water to predict when they would be married, and to whom.<sup id="cite_ref-sobotka_203-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sobotka-203">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> By the 19th century this tradition had become a festive event, and it continues today.<sup id="cite_ref-sobotka_203-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sobotka-203">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> The city council organize concerts and other events.<sup id="cite_ref-wreath_204-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wreath-204">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> Each Midsummer's Eve, apart from the official floating of wreaths, jumping over fires, and looking for the <a href="/wiki/Fern_flower" title="Fern flower">fern flower</a>, there are musical performances, dignitaries' speeches, fairs and fireworks by the river bank.<sup id="cite_ref-wreath_204-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wreath-204">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Warsaw Multimedia Fountain Park is located in an enchanting place, near the Old Town and the Vistula. The ‘Water – Light – Sound’ multimedia shows take place each Friday and Saturday from May till September at 9.30&#160;pm (May and – 9 October pm). On other weekdays, the shows do not include lasers and sound.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Film_Festival" class="mw-redirect" title="Warsaw Film Festival">Warsaw Film festival</a>, an annual festival that takes place every October.<sup id="cite_ref-wff_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wff-205">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup> Films are usually screened in their original language with Polish subtitles and participating cinemas include Kinoteka (Palace of Science and Culture), <a href="/wiki/Multikino" title="Multikino">Multikino</a> at <a href="/wiki/Z%C5%82ote_Tarasy" title="Złote Tarasy">Golden Terraces</a> and Kultura. Over 100 films are shown throughout the festival, and awards are given to the best and most popular films.<sup id="cite_ref-wff_205-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wff-205">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums_and_art_galleries">Museums and art galleries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Museums and art galleries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Museum_of_the_History_of_Polish_Jews_in_Warsaw_building_0010.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Museum_of_the_History_of_Polish_Jews_in_Warsaw_building_0010.jpg/220px-Museum_of_the_History_of_Polish_Jews_in_Warsaw_building_0010.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="105" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Museum_of_the_History_of_Polish_Jews_in_Warsaw_building_0010.jpg/330px-Museum_of_the_History_of_Polish_Jews_in_Warsaw_building_0010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Museum_of_the_History_of_Polish_Jews_in_Warsaw_building_0010.jpg/440px-Museum_of_the_History_of_Polish_Jews_in_Warsaw_building_0010.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6850" data-file-height="3272" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Museum_of_the_History_of_Polish_Jews_in_Warsaw_building_0010.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/POLIN_Museum_of_the_History_of_Polish_Jews" title="POLIN Museum of the History of Polish Jews">Museum of the History of Polish Jews</a></div></div></div>
<p>The levelling of Warsaw during the war has left gaping holes in the city's historic collections.<sup id="cite_ref-kalicki_206-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kalicki-206">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> Although a considerable number of treasures were spirited away to safety in 1939, a great number of collections from palaces and museums in the countryside were brought to Warsaw at that time as the capital was considered a safer place than some remote castle in the borderlands.<sup id="cite_ref-kalicki_206-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kalicki-206">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> Thus losses were heavy.<sup id="cite_ref-kalicki_206-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kalicki-206">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Budynek_Muzeum_Powstania_Warszawskiego_2017.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Budynek_Muzeum_Powstania_Warszawskiego_2017.jpg/220px-Budynek_Muzeum_Powstania_Warszawskiego_2017.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Budynek_Muzeum_Powstania_Warszawskiego_2017.jpg/330px-Budynek_Muzeum_Powstania_Warszawskiego_2017.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Budynek_Muzeum_Powstania_Warszawskiego_2017.jpg/440px-Budynek_Muzeum_Powstania_Warszawskiego_2017.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4429" data-file-height="3181" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Budynek_Muzeum_Powstania_Warszawskiego_2017.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Uprising_Museum" title="Warsaw Uprising Museum">Warsaw Uprising Museum</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Muzeum_Narodowe_w_Warszawie_Galeria_Sztuki_XIX_wieku.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Muzeum_Narodowe_w_Warszawie_Galeria_Sztuki_XIX_wieku.JPG/220px-Muzeum_Narodowe_w_Warszawie_Galeria_Sztuki_XIX_wieku.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Muzeum_Narodowe_w_Warszawie_Galeria_Sztuki_XIX_wieku.JPG/330px-Muzeum_Narodowe_w_Warszawie_Galeria_Sztuki_XIX_wieku.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Muzeum_Narodowe_w_Warszawie_Galeria_Sztuki_XIX_wieku.JPG/440px-Muzeum_Narodowe_w_Warszawie_Galeria_Sztuki_XIX_wieku.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4768" data-file-height="3091" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Muzeum_Narodowe_w_Warszawie_Galeria_Sztuki_XIX_wieku.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Gallery of the 19th-Century Art at the <a href="/wiki/National_Museum,_Warsaw" title="National Museum, Warsaw">National Museum</a></div></div></div>
<p>As interesting examples of expositions the most notable are: the world's first <a href="/wiki/Poster_Museum,_Wilan%C3%B3w" title="Poster Museum, Wilanów">Museum of Posters</a> boasting one of the largest collections of art <a href="/wiki/Poster" title="Poster">posters</a> in the world,<sup id="cite_ref-postermuseum_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-postermuseum-207">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> the Museum of Hunting and Riding and the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Railway_Museum" title="Warsaw Railway Museum">Railway Museum</a>. From among Warsaw's 60 museums, the most prestigious ones are the <a href="/wiki/National_Museum,_Warsaw" title="National Museum, Warsaw">National Museum</a> with a collection of works whose origin ranges in time from antiquity till the present epoch as well as one of the best collections of paintings in the country including some paintings from Adolf Hitler's private collection,<sup id="cite_ref-Schwarz_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schwarz-208">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Polish_Army_Museum" title="Polish Army Museum">Museum of the Polish Army</a> whose set portrays the history of arms.
</p><p>The collections of <a href="/wiki/%C5%81azienki_Palace" class="mw-redirect" title="Łazienki Palace">Łazienki</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wilan%C3%B3w_Palace" title="Wilanów Palace">Wilanów</a> palaces (both buildings came through the war in good shape) focus on the paintings of the "old masters", as do those of the Royal Castle which displays the <a href="/wiki/Palais_Lanckoro%C5%84ski#Lanckoroński_Collection" title="Palais Lanckoroński">Lanckoroński Collection</a> including two paintings by Rembrandt.<sup id="cite_ref-Wetering_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wetering-209">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> The Palace in <a href="/wiki/Natolin" title="Natolin">Natolin</a>, a former rural residence of Duke <a href="/wiki/Czartoryski_family" class="mw-redirect" title="Czartoryski family">Czartoryski</a>, is another venue with its interiors and park accessible to tourists.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ostrogski_Palace_Chopin_Museum_June_2010_b.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Ostrogski_Palace_Chopin_Museum_June_2010_b.jpg/220px-Ostrogski_Palace_Chopin_Museum_June_2010_b.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Ostrogski_Palace_Chopin_Museum_June_2010_b.jpg/330px-Ostrogski_Palace_Chopin_Museum_June_2010_b.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Ostrogski_Palace_Chopin_Museum_June_2010_b.jpg/440px-Ostrogski_Palace_Chopin_Museum_June_2010_b.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3140" data-file-height="2458" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ostrogski_Palace_Chopin_Museum_June_2010_b.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The 17th-century <a href="/wiki/Ostrogski_Palace" title="Ostrogski Palace">Ostrogski Castle</a> houses the <a href="/wiki/Fryderyk_Chopin_Museum" title="Fryderyk Chopin Museum">Chopin Museum</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Holding Poland's largest private collection of art, the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_John_Paul_II_Collection" title="Museum of John Paul II Collection">Carroll Porczyński Collection Museum</a><sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> displays works from such varied artists as <a href="/wiki/Paris_Bordone" title="Paris Bordone">Paris Bordone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cornelis_van_Haarlem" title="Cornelis van Haarlem">Cornelis van Haarlem</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_de_Ribera" class="mw-redirect" title="José de Ribera">José de Ribera</a>, <a href="/wiki/William-Adolphe_Bouguereau" title="William-Adolphe Bouguereau">William-Adolphe Bouguereau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pierre-Auguste_Renoir" title="Pierre-Auguste Renoir">Pierre-Auguste Renoir</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vincent_van_Gogh" title="Vincent van Gogh">Vincent van Gogh</a><sup id="cite_ref-muzeummalarstwa_211-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-muzeummalarstwa-211">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> along with some copies of masterpieces of European painting.
</p><p>A fine tribute to the fall of Warsaw and <a href="/wiki/History_of_Poland" title="History of Poland">history of Poland</a> can be found in the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Uprising_Museum" title="Warsaw Uprising Museum">Warsaw Uprising Museum</a> and in the <a href="/wiki/Katyn_massacre" title="Katyn massacre">Katyń</a> Museum which preserves the memory of that crime.<sup id="cite_ref-Baker_212-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Baker-212">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> The Warsaw Uprising Museum also operates a rare preserved and operating historic stereoscopic theatre, the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Fotoplastikon" title="Warsaw Fotoplastikon">Warsaw Fotoplastikon</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Independence" title="Museum of Independence">Museum of Independence</a> preserves patriotic and political objects connected with Poland's struggles for independence. Dating back to 1936 the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Warsaw" title="Museum of Warsaw">Warsaw Historical Museum</a> contains 60 rooms which host a permanent exhibition of the history of Warsaw from its origins until today.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Warszawa,_pl._Ma%C5%82achowskiego_3_20170516_003.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Warszawa%2C_pl._Ma%C5%82achowskiego_3_20170516_003.jpg/220px-Warszawa%2C_pl._Ma%C5%82achowskiego_3_20170516_003.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Warszawa%2C_pl._Ma%C5%82achowskiego_3_20170516_003.jpg/330px-Warszawa%2C_pl._Ma%C5%82achowskiego_3_20170516_003.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Warszawa%2C_pl._Ma%C5%82achowskiego_3_20170516_003.jpg/440px-Warszawa%2C_pl._Ma%C5%82achowskiego_3_20170516_003.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5996" data-file-height="4003" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Warszawa,_pl._Ma%C5%82achowskiego_3_20170516_003.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Zach%C4%99ta" title="Zachęta">Zachęta</a> National Gallery of Art</div></div></div>
<p>The 17th century Royal <a href="/wiki/Ujazd%C3%B3w_Castle" title="Ujazdów Castle">Ujazdów Castle</a> currently houses the Centre for Contemporary Art, with some permanent and temporary exhibitions, concerts, shows and creative workshops. The Centre currently realizes about 500 projects a year. The <a href="/wiki/Zach%C4%99ta" title="Zachęta">Zachęta</a> National Gallery of Art, the oldest exhibition site in Warsaw, with a tradition stretching back to the mid-19th century organises exhibitions of <a href="/wiki/Modern_art" title="Modern art">modern art</a> by Polish and <a href="/wiki/International_Artists" title="International Artists">International Artists</a> and promotes art in many other ways. Since 2011, Warsaw Gallery Weekend is held on the last weekend of September.
</p><p>The city also possesses some oddities such as the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Caricature,_Warsaw" title="Museum of Caricature, Warsaw">Museum of Caricature</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Exhibitions_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Exhibitions-213">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_John_Paul_II_and_Primate_Wyszy%C5%84ski" title="Museum of John Paul II and Primate Wyszyński">Museum of John Paul II and Primate Wyszyński</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Legia_Warsaw_Museum" title="Legia Warsaw Museum">Legia Warsaw Museum</a>, and a Motorisation Museum in <a href="/wiki/Otr%C4%99busy" title="Otrębusy">Otrębusy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-motoryzacji_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-motoryzacji-214">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_and_film">Media and film</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Media and film">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_films_featuring_Warsaw" class="mw-redirect" title="List of films featuring Warsaw">List of films featuring Warsaw</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Siedziba_Telewizji_Polskiej_w_Warszawie_2017.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Siedziba_Telewizji_Polskiej_w_Warszawie_2017.jpg/220px-Siedziba_Telewizji_Polskiej_w_Warszawie_2017.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Siedziba_Telewizji_Polskiej_w_Warszawie_2017.jpg/330px-Siedziba_Telewizji_Polskiej_w_Warszawie_2017.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Siedziba_Telewizji_Polskiej_w_Warszawie_2017.jpg/440px-Siedziba_Telewizji_Polskiej_w_Warszawie_2017.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6940" data-file-height="4605" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Siedziba_Telewizji_Polskiej_w_Warszawie_2017.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Main <a href="/wiki/Telewizja_Polska" title="Telewizja Polska">TVP</a> headquarters at Woronicza street</div></div></div>
<p>Warsaw is the media centre of Poland, and the location of the main headquarters of <a href="/wiki/Telewizja_Polska" title="Telewizja Polska">TVP</a> and other numerous local and national TV and <a href="/wiki/Radio_broadcasting" title="Radio broadcasting">radio stations</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Polskie_Radio" title="Polskie Radio">Polskie Radio</a> (Polish Radio), <a href="/wiki/TVN_(Poland)" class="mw-redirect" title="TVN (Poland)">TVN</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polsat" title="Polsat">Polsat</a>, <a href="/wiki/TV4_(Poland)" class="mw-redirect" title="TV4 (Poland)">TV4</a>, <a href="/wiki/TV_Puls" title="TV Puls">TV Puls</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canal%2B_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="Canal+ Poland">Canal+ Poland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cyfra%2B" class="mw-redirect" title="Cyfra+">Cyfra+</a> and <a href="/wiki/MTV_Poland" class="mw-redirect" title="MTV Poland">MTV Poland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-broadbandtvnews_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-broadbandtvnews-215">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since May 1661 the first Polish newspaper, the <i><a href="/wiki/Merkuriusz_Polski_Ordynaryjny" title="Merkuriusz Polski Ordynaryjny">Polish Ordinary Mercury</a></i>, was printed in Warsaw. The city is also the printing capital of Poland with a wide variety of domestic and foreign periodicals expressing diverse views, and domestic newspapers are extremely competitive. <i><a href="/wiki/Rzeczpospolita_(newspaper)" title="Rzeczpospolita (newspaper)">Rzeczpospolita</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Gazeta_Wyborcza" title="Gazeta Wyborcza">Gazeta Wyborcza</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Dziennik_Polska-Europa-%C5%9Awiat" title="Dziennik Polska-Europa-Świat">Dziennik Polska-Europa-Świat</a></i>, Poland's large nationwide daily newspapers,<sup id="cite_ref-instytut_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-instytut-216">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> have their headquarters in Warsaw.
</p><p>Warsaw also has a sizable movie and television industry. The city houses several movie companies and <a href="/wiki/Movie_studio" class="mw-redirect" title="Movie studio">studios</a>. Among the movie companies are TOR, Czołówka, Zebra and <a href="/wiki/KADR_(studio)" title="KADR (studio)">Kadr</a> which is behind several international movie productions.<sup id="cite_ref-pisf_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pisf-217">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Over the next few years the new Film City in <a href="/wiki/Nowe_Miasto_nad_Pilic%C4%85" title="Nowe Miasto nad Pilicą">Nowe Miasto</a>, located a mere 80&#160;km (50&#160;mi) from Warsaw, will become the centre of <a href="/wiki/Cinema_of_Poland" title="Cinema of Poland">Polish film</a> production and international co-production.<sup id="cite_ref-pisf_217-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pisf-217">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> It is to be the largest high-tech film studio in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-pisf_217-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pisf-217">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> The first projects filmed in the new Film City will be two films about the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_uprising" class="mw-redirect" title="Warsaw uprising">Warsaw uprising</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-pisf_217-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pisf-217">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> Two <a href="/wiki/Backlot" title="Backlot">backlots</a> will be constructed for these projects&#160;– a lot of pre-World War II Warsaw and city ruins.<sup id="cite_ref-pisf_217-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pisf-217">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since World War II, Warsaw has been the most important centre of film production in Poland. It has also been featured in numerous movies, both Polish and foreign, for example: <a href="/wiki/Kana%C5%82_(film)" class="mw-redirect" title="Kanał (film)"><i>Kanał</i></a> and <i><a href="/wiki/Korczak_(film)" title="Korczak (film)">Korczak</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Andrzej_Wajda" title="Andrzej Wajda">Andrzej Wajda</a> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Decalogue_(film)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Decalogue (film)">The Decalogue</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Krzysztof_Kie%C5%9Blowski" title="Krzysztof Kieślowski">Krzysztof Kieślowski</a>, also including <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy Award">Oscar</a> winner <a href="/wiki/The_Pianist_(2002_film)" title="The Pianist (2002 film)"><i>The Pianist</i></a> by <a href="/wiki/Roman_Polanski" title="Roman Polanski">Roman Polański</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-thepianistmovie_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thepianistmovie-218">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>It is also home to the National Film Archive, which, since 1955, has been collecting and preserving Polish film culture.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Warsaw" title="Sport in Warsaw">Sport in Warsaw</a></div>
<p>On 9 April 2008 the President of Warsaw, <a href="/wiki/Hanna_Gronkiewicz-Waltz" title="Hanna Gronkiewicz-Waltz">Hanna Gronkiewicz-Waltz</a>, obtained from the mayor of <a href="/wiki/Stuttgart" title="Stuttgart">Stuttgart</a> <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Schuster" title="Wolfgang Schuster">Wolfgang Schuster</a> a challenge award&#160;– a <a href="/wiki/Commemorative_plaque" title="Commemorative plaque">commemorative plaque</a> awarded to Warsaw as the European capital of Sport in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Warsaw_National_Stadium_before_Germany_-_Italy_(6).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Warsaw_National_Stadium_before_Germany_-_Italy_%286%29.jpg/220px-Warsaw_National_Stadium_before_Germany_-_Italy_%286%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Warsaw_National_Stadium_before_Germany_-_Italy_%286%29.jpg/330px-Warsaw_National_Stadium_before_Germany_-_Italy_%286%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e6/Warsaw_National_Stadium_before_Germany_-_Italy_%286%29.jpg/440px-Warsaw_National_Stadium_before_Germany_-_Italy_%286%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Warsaw_National_Stadium_before_Germany_-_Italy_(6).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Interior of the <a href="/wiki/National_Stadium_(Warsaw)" class="mw-redirect" title="National Stadium (Warsaw)">National Stadium</a> before the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012" title="UEFA Euro 2012">UEFA Euro 2012</a> semi-final match between <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">Germany</a> and <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_football_team" title="Italy national football team">Italy</a> on 28 June 2012</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Stadium_(Warsaw)" class="mw-redirect" title="National Stadium (Warsaw)">National Stadium</a>, a 58,500-seat-capacity football (soccer) stadium, replaced Warsaw's recently demolished <a href="/wiki/10th-Anniversary_Stadium" title="10th-Anniversary Stadium">10th-Anniversary Stadium</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup> The national stadium hosted the opening match, 2 group matches, a quarterfinal, and a semi-final of the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2012" title="UEFA Euro 2012">UEFA Euro 2012</a> hosted jointly by Poland and <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Moderne_wolkenkrabber_Warschau_0865.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Moderne_wolkenkrabber_Warschau_0865.PNG/220px-Moderne_wolkenkrabber_Warschau_0865.PNG" decoding="async" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Moderne_wolkenkrabber_Warschau_0865.PNG/330px-Moderne_wolkenkrabber_Warschau_0865.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Moderne_wolkenkrabber_Warschau_0865.PNG/440px-Moderne_wolkenkrabber_Warschau_0865.PNG 2x" data-file-width="731" data-file-height="541" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Moderne_wolkenkrabber_Warschau_0865.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Olympic Center</div></div></div>
<p>There are many sports centres in the city as well. Most of these facilities are swimming pools and sports halls, many of them built by the municipality in the past several years. The main indoor venue is <a href="/wiki/Torwar_Hall" class="mw-redirect" title="Torwar Hall">Hala Torwar</a>, used for all kinds of indoor sports (it was a venue for the <a href="/wiki/2009_EuroBasket" class="mw-redirect" title="2009 EuroBasket">2009 EuroBasket</a><sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> but it is also used as an indoor skating rink). There is also an open-air skating rink (Stegny) and a horse racetrack (Służewiec).
</p><p>The best of the city's swimming centres is at Wodny Park Warszawianka, 4&#160;km (2&#160;mi) south of the centre at Merliniego Street, where there's an Olympic-sized pool as well as water slides and children's areas.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>From the Warsovian football teams, the most famous is <a href="/wiki/Legia_Warsaw" title="Legia Warsaw">Legia Warsaw</a>&#160;– the army club with a nationwide following play at <a href="/wiki/Polish_Army_Stadium" title="Polish Army Stadium">Polish Army Stadium</a>, just southeast of the centre at <a href="/wiki/%C5%81azienkowska_Street" class="mw-redirect" title="Łazienkowska Street">Łazienkowska Street</a>. Established in 1916, they have won the <a href="/wiki/Ekstraklasa" title="Ekstraklasa">country's championship</a> 13 times (most recently in 2018) and won the <a href="/wiki/Polish_Cup" title="Polish Cup">Polish Cup</a> 19 times. In the Champions League season 1995/96 they reached the quarter-finals, where they lost to <a href="/wiki/Panathinaikos_F.C." title="Panathinaikos F.C.">Panathinaikos</a> Athens.
</p><p>Their local rivals, <a href="/wiki/Polonia_Warsaw" title="Polonia Warsaw">Polonia Warsaw</a>, have significantly fewer supporters, yet they managed to win the country's championship two times (in 1946 and 2000) and won the cup twice as well. Polonia's home venue is located at Konwiktorska Street, a ten-minute walk north from the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Old_Town" title="Warsaw Old Town">Old Town</a>. Polonia was relegated from the country's top flight in 2013 because of their disastrous financial situation. They are now playing in the second league (3rd tier in Poland).
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Legia_Warszawa_(basketball)" title="Legia Warszawa (basketball)">Legia Warsaw's basketball team</a> was one of the country's best teams in 50s and 60s. They are now participating in <a href="/wiki/Polish_Basketball_League" title="Polish Basketball League">PLK</a>, the highest-tier level of the Polish basketball.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Warsaw_Mermaid">Warsaw Mermaid</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Warsaw Mermaid">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Warsaw" title="Coat of arms of Warsaw">Coat of arms of Warsaw</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Warsaw_Sirene_1659.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Warsaw_Sirene_1659.PNG/170px-Warsaw_Sirene_1659.PNG" decoding="async" width="170" height="219" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/99/Warsaw_Sirene_1659.PNG 1.5x" data-file-width="235" data-file-height="303" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Warsaw_Sirene_1659.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The 1659 <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Warsaw" title="Coat of arms of Warsaw">coat of arms of Old Warsaw</a> on the cover of one of Warsaw's accounting books</div></div></div>
<p>The mermaid (<i>syrenka</i>) is Warsaw's symbol<sup id="cite_ref-ucl_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ucl-225">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> and can be found on statues throughout the city and on <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Warsaw" title="Coat of arms of Warsaw">the city's coat of arms</a>. This imagery has been in use since at least the mid-14th century.<sup id="cite_ref-Mermaid_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mermaid-226">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> The oldest existing armed seal of Warsaw is from the year 1390, consisting of a round seal bordered with the Latin inscription <i>Sigilium Civitatis Varsoviensis</i> (Seal of the city of Warsaw).<sup id="cite_ref-herb_227-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-herb-227">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup> City records as far back as 1609 document the use of a crude form of a <a href="/wiki/Sea_monster" title="Sea monster">sea monster</a> with a female upper body and holding a sword in its claws.<sup id="cite_ref-Bratosiewicz_228-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bratosiewicz-228">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> In 1653 the poet Zygmunt Laukowski asks the question:
</p>
<table class="rquote pullquote floatcenter" role="presentation" style="border-collapse:collapse; border-style:none; float:center; margin:0.5em 0.75em; width:33%;">

<tbody><tr style="text-align:left; vertical-align:top;">
<td style="color:#b2b7f2; font-size:3.3em; font-family:&#39;Times New Roman&#39;,serif; font-weight:bold; padding:4px 2px 2px; width:0.5em; line-height: 1em;">“
</td>
<td style="padding:0 10px;">Warsaw of strong walls; why was the emblem Mermaid with sharp sword, given you by the kings?
</td>
<td style="color:#b2b7f2; font-size:3.3em; font-family:&#39;Times New Roman&#39;,serif; font-weight:bold; padding:4px 2px 2px; text-align:right; vertical-align:bottom; width:0.5em; line-height: 1em;">”
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td class="rquotecite" colspan="3" style="padding-top:10px; font-size:smaller; line-height:normal; text-align:right;"><cite>—&#160;Zygmunt Laukowski<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup></cite>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Syrenka_Warszawska.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Syrenka_Warszawska.jpg/170px-Syrenka_Warszawska.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="204" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Syrenka_Warszawska.jpg/255px-Syrenka_Warszawska.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Syrenka_Warszawska.jpg/340px-Syrenka_Warszawska.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1067" data-file-height="1282" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Syrenka_Warszawska.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>1855 bronze sculpture of <i>The Warsaw Mermaid</i> in the <a href="/wiki/Old_Town_Market_Place,_Warsaw" title="Old Town Market Place, Warsaw">Old Town Market Place</a></div></div></div>
<p>The Mermaid Statue stands in the very centre of Old Town Square, surrounded by a fountain. Due to vandalism, the original statue had been moved to the grounds of the Museum of Warsaw – the statue in the square is a copy.
This is not the only mermaid in Warsaw. Another is located on the bank of the Vistula River near Świętokrzyski Bridge and another on Karowa Street.
</p><p>The origin of the legendary figure is not fully known. The best-known legend, by Artur Oppman, is that long ago two of <a href="/wiki/Triton_(mythology)" title="Triton (mythology)">Triton</a>'s daughters set out on a journey through the depths of the oceans and seas. One of them decided to stay on the coast of Denmark and can be seen sitting at the entrance to the port of <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen" title="Copenhagen">Copenhagen</a>. The second mermaid reached the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/Vistula" title="Vistula">Vistula</a> River and plunged into its waters. She stopped to rest on a sandy beach by the village of Warszowa, where fishermen came to admire her beauty and listen to her beautiful voice. A greedy merchant also heard her songs; he followed the fishermen and captured the mermaid.<sup id="cite_ref-legend_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-legend-230">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Another legend says that a mermaid once swam to Warsaw from the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic Sea</a> for the love of the Griffin, the ancient defender of the city, who was killed in a struggle against the <a href="/wiki/Deluge_(history)" title="Deluge (history)">Swedish invasions</a> of the 17th century. The mermaid, wishing to avenge his death, took the position of defender of Warsaw, becoming the symbol of the city.<sup id="cite_ref-legend_230-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-legend-230">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Every member of the <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Royal_Hussars" title="Queen&#39;s Royal Hussars">Queen's Royal Hussars</a> of the UK's light <a href="/wiki/Cavalry" title="Cavalry">cavalry</a> wears the <i>Maid of Warsaw</i>, the crest of the City of Warsaw, on the left sleeve of his No. 2 (Service) Dress.<sup id="cite_ref-qohmuseum_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qohmuseum-231">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> Members of <a href="/wiki/No._651_Squadron_RAF" title="No. 651 Squadron RAF">651 Squadron Army Air Corps</a> of the United Kingdom also wear the <i>Maid of Warsaw</i> on the left sleeve of their No. 2 (Service) Dress.<sup id="cite_ref-RAF_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RAF-232">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Famous_people">Famous people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Famous people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Category:People_from_Warsaw" title="Category:People from Warsaw">Category:People from Warsaw</a></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r923042769/mw-parser-output/.tmulti"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;max-width:242px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:119px;max-width:119px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:165px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:Marie_Curie_1903.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Marie_Curie_1903.jpg/117px-Marie_Curie_1903.jpg" decoding="async" width="117" style="width:119px;max-width:119px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:165px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:Benoit_Mandelbrot,_TED_2010.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Benoit_Mandelbrot%2C_TED_2010.jpg/117px-Benoit_Mandelbrot%2C_TED_2010.jpg" decoding="async" width="117" height="166" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Benoit_Mandelbrot%2C_TED_2010.jpg/176px-Benoit_Mandelbrot%2C_TED_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Benoit_Mandelbrot%2C_TED_2010.jpg/234px-Benoit_Mandelbrot%2C_TED_2010.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3744" data-file-height="5322" /></a></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:126px;max-width:126px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:160px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:Samuel_Goldwyn_-_Jul_1919_EH.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Samuel_Goldwyn_-_Jul_1919_EH.jpg/124px-Samuel_Goldwyn_-_Jul_1919_EH.jpg" decoding="async" width="124" height="160" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Samuel_Goldwyn_-_Jul_1919_EH.jpg/186px-Samuel_Goldwyn_-_Jul_1919_EH.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Samuel_Goldwyn_-_Jul_1919_EH.jpg/248px-Samuel_Goldwyn_-_Jul_1919_EH.jpg 2x" data-file-width="568" data-file-height="734" /></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:112px;max-width:112px"><div class="thumbimage" style="height:160px;overflow:hidden"><a href="/wiki/File:Tamara_%C5%81empicka_ssj_20060914_-_cropped.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Tamara_%C5%81empicka_ssj_20060914_-_cropped.jpg/110px-Tamara_%C5%81empicka_ssj_20060914_-_cropped.jpg" decoding="async" width="110" height="161" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Tamara_%C5%81empicka_ssj_20060914_-_cropped.jpg/165px-Tamara_%C5%81empicka_ssj_20060914_-_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Tamara_%C5%81empicka_ssj_20060914_-_cropped.jpg/220px-Tamara_%C5%81empicka_ssj_20060914_-_cropped.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1240" data-file-height="1812" /></a></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="thumbcaption" style="background-color:transparent">Famous notables born in Warsaw, clockwise from upper left: <a href="/wiki/Maria_Sk%C5%82odowska-Curie" class="mw-redirect" title="Maria Skłodowska-Curie">Maria Skłodowska-Curie</a>, <a href="/wiki/Benoit_Mandelbrot" title="Benoit Mandelbrot">Benoit Mandelbrot</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Goldwyn" title="Samuel Goldwyn">Samuel Goldwyn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tamara_de_Lempicka" title="Tamara de Lempicka">Tamara de Lempicka</a></div></div></div></div>
<p>One of the most famous people born in Warsaw was <a href="/wiki/Marie_Curie" title="Marie Curie">Maria Skłodowska-Curie</a>, who achieved international recognition for her research on radioactivity and was the first female recipient of the Nobel Prize.<sup id="cite_ref-nobelprize_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nobelprize-233">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> Famous musicians include <a href="/wiki/W%C5%82adys%C5%82aw_Szpilman" title="Władysław Szpilman">Władysław Szpilman</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fr%C3%A9d%C3%A9ric_Chopin" title="Frédéric Chopin">Frédéric Chopin</a>. Though Chopin was born in the village of <a href="/wiki/%C5%BBelazowa_Wola" title="Żelazowa Wola">Żelazowa Wola</a>, about 60&#160;km (37&#160;mi) from Warsaw, he moved to the city with his family when he was seven months old.<sup id="cite_ref-Lawrynowicz_234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lawrynowicz-234">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Casimir_Pulaski" title="Casimir Pulaski">Casimir Pulaski</a>, a Polish general and hero of the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a>, was born here in 1745.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Tamara_de_Lempicka" title="Tamara de Lempicka">Tamara de Lempicka</a> was a famous artist born in Warsaw.<sup id="cite_ref-lempicka_236-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lempicka-236">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> She was born Maria Górska in Warsaw to wealthy parents and in 1916 married a Polish lawyer Tadeusz Łempicki.<sup id="cite_ref-marchand_237-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-marchand-237">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup> Better than anyone else she represented the <a href="/wiki/Art_deco" class="mw-redirect" title="Art deco">art deco</a> style in painting and art.<sup id="cite_ref-lempicka_236-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lempicka-236">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup>
<a href="/wiki/Nathan_Alterman" title="Nathan Alterman">Nathan Alterman</a>, the Israeli poet, was born in Warsaw, as was <a href="/wiki/Moshe_Vilenski" class="mw-redirect" title="Moshe Vilenski">Moshe Vilenski</a>, the Israeli composer, lyricist, and pianist, who studied music at the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Conservatory" class="mw-redirect" title="Warsaw Conservatory">Warsaw Conservatory</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-jewishvirtuallibrary1_238-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jewishvirtuallibrary1-238">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russian Jewish</a> poet and essayist <a href="/wiki/Osip_Mandelstam" title="Osip Mandelstam">Osip Mandelstam</a>, one of the foremost members of the <a href="/wiki/Acmeist_poetry" title="Acmeist poetry">Acmeist</a> school of poetry was born in Warsaw while it was part of the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a>. Other notables include <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Goldwyn" title="Samuel Goldwyn">Samuel Goldwyn</a>, the founder of <a href="/wiki/Goldwyn_Pictures" title="Goldwyn Pictures">Goldwyn Pictures</a>, mathematician <a href="/wiki/Benoit_Mandelbrot" title="Benoit Mandelbrot">Benoit Mandelbrot</a>, physicist <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Rotblat" title="Joseph Rotblat">Joseph Rotblat</a> and biochemist <a href="/wiki/Casimir_Funk" title="Casimir Funk">Casimir Funk</a>. Warsaw was the beloved city of <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Bashevis_Singer" title="Isaac Bashevis Singer">Isaac Bashevis Singer</a>, which he described in many of his novels:<sup id="cite_ref-jewish-theatre_239-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jewish-theatre-239">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> "Warsaw has just now been destroyed. No one will ever see the Warsaw I knew. Let me just write about it. Let this Warsaw not disappear forever", he wrote.<sup id="cite_ref-Burgin_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Burgin-240">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">International relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: International relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns_and_sister_cities">Twin towns and sister cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Twin towns and sister cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_twin_towns_and_sister_cities_in_Poland" title="List of twin towns and sister cities in Poland">List of twin towns and sister cities in Poland</a></div>
<p>Warsaw is <a href="/wiki/Twin_towns_and_sister_cities" class="mw-redirect" title="Twin towns and sister cities">twinned</a> with:<sup id="cite_ref-Warsaw_241-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Warsaw-241">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 22em; -webkit-column-width: 22em; column-width: 22em;">
<ul><li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany"><img alt="Germany" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/23px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/35px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/46px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a> in Germany <small><i>(since 1991)</i></small><sup id="cite_ref-Berlin_twinnings_242-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Berlin_twinnings-242">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup></li>

<td style="color:#b2b7f2; font-size:3.3em; font-family:&#39;Times New Roman&#39;,serif; font-weight:bold; padding:4px 2px 2px; width:0.5em; line-height: 1em;">“
</td>
<td style="padding:0 10px;">City of menace, like a coffin lid<br /> thrown down an abyss as if<br /> by a tempest's blow –<br /> yet proud<br /> as a black lion who takes long to die
</td>
<td style="color:#b2b7f2; font-size:3.3em; font-family:&#39;Times New Roman&#39;,serif; font-weight:bold; padding:4px 2px 2px; text-align:right; vertical-align:bottom; width:0.5em; line-height: 1em;">”

<td style="color:#b2b7f2; font-size:3.3em; font-family:&#39;Times New Roman&#39;,serif; font-weight:bold; padding:4px 2px 2px; width:0.5em; line-height: 1em;">“
</td>
<td style="padding:0 10px;">What are you doing here, poet, on the ruins<br /> Of St. John's Cathedral this sunny<br /> Day in spring?<br /> What are you thinking here, where the wind<br /> Blowing from the Vistula scatters<br /> The red dust of the rubble?
</td>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Warsaw&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="navigation" aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">

<li id="cite_note-New_Zoo_Revue-104"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-New_Zoo_Revue_104-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Warsaw Zoo opened 11 March 1928, on Ratuszowa Street. It was not the first <a href="/wiki/Zoo" title="Zoo">zoological</a> garden in Warsaw; King <a href="/wiki/John_III_Sobieski" title="John III Sobieski">Jan Sobieski III</a> kept a court menagerie in <a href="/wiki/Wilan%C3%B3w" title="Wilanów">Wilanów</a>. Several private zoos were also established in Warsaw in the 19th century. <cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20050118091706/http://www.warsawvoice.pl/view/2044/">"New Zoo Revue"</a>. <i>warsawvoice.pl</i>. 24 April 2003.
